The v3.1 body is **not discarded**. It remains the preserved conceptual and historical encyclopedia body. This supplement becomes the new current-state reader spine placed above it.

```yaml
current_runtime_base:
  id: V96_FULL_CONSOLIDATED_RUNTIME
  role: full project-root candidate supplied in this chat
  boundary: compact/productized runtime root, not complete forensic archive
  key_claims_from_report:
    - consolidates V88 base and V90-V95 update stack
    - restores shell-root invariant files
    - establishes `/ion` as canonical Cursor command
    - treats Cursor parent chat as carrier-control surface
    - requires every spawned row to have context package, compiled bundle, context-load receipt, and CONTEXT PROOF contract
    - full local pytest was not claimed

overlay_line:
  V97:
    role: lead-dev survival audit and autonomous-loop recovery plan
    controlling_rule: stop expansion until minimal autonomous loop survival proof exists
  V98:
    role: master orchestration, automation, template enforcement, and UI recovery plan
    controlling_rule: automation/template/steward/UI must be enforced by commands, receipts, and cockpit-visible state
  V99:
    role: agent context continuity, timeline, route-map, and runtime separation design
    controlling_rule: agents are governed context systems with route maps, rolling context windows, timelines, and deltas
  V100:
    role: living encyclopedia maintenance and process integration
    controlling_rule: the encyclopedia is a maintained ION state object and must update whenever branch authority, runtime proof, context law, or product boundary changes
```

The current operational center is therefore no longer “V41/V42 candidate encyclopedia line.” The current center is:

```text
V96 productized runtime base
+ V97 survival audit
+ V98 autonomous-loop/template/steward/UI recovery plan
+ V99 agent context continuity and runtime separation design
+ V100 living encyclopedia maintenance integration
```

# 2. What v3.1 Still Governs

The v3.1 encyclopedia remains strong and should stay inside ION because it preserves the doctrine that made the project coherent:

```text
Maintained Work Surface
Front-Stage Council
Representational Integrity
Persona latency lanes
Expressive telemetry
Visual Perception and Interaction Agent
Front-Stage Council Runtime Receipts
Conversational repair
Non-production boundary discipline
```

The following v3.1 rules remain live doctrine unless explicitly superseded by a later ratified protocol:

```text
1. ION remains NOT_PRODUCTION_READY until proven otherwise.
2. Persona is not all of ION.
3. User-facing claims require grounding, authority, emission permission, visibility level, and repair obligations.
4. No false certainty; no false uncertainty.
5. Rendered behavior is part of truth.
6. Corrections are continuity events, not merely apologies.
7. Chat correction does not equal artifact correction.
8. Candidate files are not live files until patched into the correct project root and verified.
```

The v3.1 limitation is not conceptual weakness. The limitation is **staleness against the current supplied runtime line**. It must now be read as preserved foundation plus historical/current doctrine, not as the latest branch map.

---

# 3. New Current-State Override

Where the preserved v3.1 body says the current live project line is `V41_FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_RUNTIME_RECEIPTS`, read that as historical for the supplied v3.1 artifact.

For the current supplied project line in this chat, the live interpretation is:

```text
V96_FULL_CONSOLIDATED_RUNTIME is the current full base.
V97, V98, and V99 are overlays to apply after V96.
V100 adds encyclopedia maintenance integration as another overlay.
```

Where the preserved body says `V42_CONVERSATIONAL_RECEIPTS_AND_LIVE_REPAIR` is a candidate next branch, read that within the v3.1 historical boundary. The current V96 root contains later material and must be inspected directly for actual live V42 status before claiming implementation completeness.

Where the preserved body describes production gates, keep the production-gate namespace discipline. Do not collapse branch numbers, production gates, documentary versions, overlay versions, and release-candidate versions into one sequence.

---

# 4. Living Encyclopedia Law

The encyclopedia is now a maintained ION state object. It must no longer live as a detached explanation file.

## 4.1 Required location

The current living encyclopedia master should live at:

```text
ION/docs/encyclopedia/ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v4_0_LIVE_V96_V100_CONTEXT_SYSTEM_AND_AUTONOMOUS_LOOP_RECOVERY.md
```

Its maintenance protocol should live at:

```text
ION/02_architecture/ION_LIVING_ENCYCLOPEDIA_MAINTENANCE_PROTOCOL.md
```

Its current manifest should live at:

```text
ION/05_context/current/ION_LIVING_ENCYCLOPEDIA_MANIFEST_V100.json
```

Its update receipt should live at:

```text
ION/05_context/signals/v100_living_encyclopedia_maintenance_receipt_20260501.txt
```

## 4.2 Required triggers

A living encyclopedia update is required when any of the following changes:

```text
1. the current runtime base changes;
2. an overlay becomes part of the accepted stack;
3. the canonical command or mount path changes;
4. agent context package law changes;
5. template/action proof law changes;
6. Steward integration law changes;
7. cockpit/JOC visibility law changes;
8. production-readiness verdict changes;
9. a former candidate branch becomes live implementation;
10. a major older encyclopedia statement becomes stale against inspected project evidence.
```

## 4.3 Required shape of future updates

Every future encyclopedia update must include:

```text
CURRENT_STATE_OVERRIDE
SOURCE_ARTIFACTS_AND_HASHES
CLAIM_LEDGER
WHAT_REMAINS_TRUE_FROM_PRIOR_BODY
WHAT_IS_STALE_OR_HISTORICAL
NEW VERSION/GATE MAP
RUNTIME PROOF CLAIMS AND NON-CLAIMS
NEXT LAWFUL MAINTENANCE MOVE
```

## 4.4 Forbidden encyclopedia behavior

The encyclopedia must not:

```text
claim production readiness from documentation coherence;
claim full project verification from focused or partial tests;
claim an overlay is a full root;
treat Cursor/MCP/API carrier behavior as ION authority by itself;
preserve stale current-state language without an override;
erase historical material that explains why the current law exists;
split branch numbers, gates, and docs versions without a namespace map;
be updated in chat only without a repo-addressed file and receipt.
```

---

# 5. Context-System Update to the Encyclopedia

The v3.1 encyclopedia already explained Persona, Relay, Steward, maintained work surfaces, repairs, and claim receipts. V99 adds the missing context-system spine:

```text
Main Context Package
+ rolling context windows
+ route-deeper map
+ per-role context timeline
+ template/action proof
+ context delta writeback
+ lead-dev carrier context control surface
+ runtime/core/state/archive separation
```

This means the encyclopedia must now describe ION as not only a maintained work surface, but a **maintained context-surface runtime**:

```text
ION turns AI work into maintained state by compiling role-specific context packages, routing attention through explicit context windows, enforcing template/action contracts, validating returns through proof gates, integrating accepted deltas into Steward state, and projecting the result into navigable timelines and cockpit-visible surfaces.
```

The current agent-context law is:

```text
An ION agent is not a prompt, not a persona, not a boot-file chain, and not a loose subagent.
An ION agent is a governed context system mounted through a compiled role context bundle with authority, mission, routes, budgets, template/action proof, receipt requirements, and delta writeback.
```

---

# 6. Runtime Separation Update

The v3.1 encyclopedia was mostly documentary. V84/V96/V99 make runtime separation a central project law.

The current packaging model should distinguish:

```text
runtime_core:
  kernel modules, CLI entrypoints, active registries, active templates, active protocols

runtime_state:
  current spawn plans, context packages, context windows, queues, signals, receipts, work packets

execution_cycles:
  generated role returns, accepted/rejected packets, run receipts, continuation packets

ui_surface:
  JOC/cockpit view models, operator status, command previews, proof visibility

historical_archive:
  older branches, donor zips, forensic evidence, prior encyclopedia bodies

release_overlay:
  small patch/update zips such as V97, V98, V99, and V100
```

The compact productized runtime should not require the full historical archive to operate. The historical archive remains critical for forensic reconstruction, but it must not be treated as live authority over the current root.

---

# 7. Autonomous-Loop Survival Gate

The v3.1 encyclopedia could teach ION. The V96/V97/V98/V99 line demands that ION now prove it can run.

The next survival gate remains:

```text
kernel.ion_autonomous_loop
```

The first implementation should be local and deterministic. It does not need external LLM execution to prove the loop mechanics. It must prove:

```text
goal intake
→ context package selection/compilation
→ template/action gate
→ simulated or bounded worker return
→ CONTEXT PROOF validation
→ TEMPLATE ACTION PROOF validation
→ Steward integration
→ receipt
→ cockpit/status projection
→ next stop reason or next work packet
```

Until this exists, ION may claim rich architecture and partial runtime surfaces, but it must not claim autonomous operation.

---

# 8. Updated One-Page Product Definition

ION is a governed runtime for AI-mediated work that converts intent, context, templates, roles, evidence, claims, repairs, and execution returns into maintained, inspectable state.

Its product form is:

```text
ION turns AI collaboration into a maintained work and context surface.
```

Its technical form is:

```text
ION compiles role-specific context packages, routes work through template/action contracts, validates returns through proof gates, integrates accepted deltas into Steward-controlled state, and projects the resulting work surface into human-visible cockpit and continuity artifacts.
```

Its survival proof form is:

```text
ION is real when a weak carrier can invoke one command and the system advances lawful work without the user micromanaging agents, context loading, template choice, or state integration.
```

---

# 10. Next Lawful Maintenance Move

The next ION work should not be another conceptual expansion. The correct next sequence is:

```text
1. Apply V100 over the current V96+V97+V98+V99 root.
2. Keep v3.1 preserved under the v4.0 supplement.
3. Implement the minimal host-independent autonomous loop.
4. Add template/action gate tests.
5. Add Steward integration tests.
6. Project autonomous-loop status into current context/cockpit state.
7. Only then re-open Cursor/MCP/API carrier integration.
```

The encyclopedia should then be updated again with actual command/test evidence from that autonomous-loop implementation.

---

# 11. v4.0 Settlement

```yaml
settled:
  - the encyclopedia must remain part of ION as a maintained process artifact
  - v3.1 is preserved as foundation and historical/current doctrine for V41/V42
  - V96 is treated as the current full runtime base supplied in this chat
  - V97/V98/V99 are treated as overlays to that base
  - V100 adds the living encyclopedia maintenance layer
  - production readiness remains false
  - autonomous operation remains unclaimed until kernel.ion_autonomous_loop or equivalent survival proof passes

not_settled:
  - whether the current full root passes the complete test suite
  - whether V42 is fully live and verified in the current V96 root
  - final production-gate namespace implementation status
  - implementation of the host-independent autonomous loop
  - final archive-vs-runtime packaging policy after full consolidation
```

# 2. How to Read This Encyclopedia

Read this edition in four layers.

## 2.1 Current-State Layer

The current-state layer is authoritative for interpreting the rest of the document. It describes the current supplied live project evidence as V41 and corrects older V33/V35/V36 language where needed.

Primary concepts:

```text
Maintained Work Surface
Front-Stage Council
Front-Stage Council Runtime Receipts
Visual Perception and Interaction Agent
V42 Conversational Receipts and Live Repair
```

## 2.2 Historical Body Layer

The historical v2.0 body remains valuable, but it must be read as lineage and design record. It should not override the V41 live re-anchor.

## 2.3 Candidate Implementation Layer

The V42 seed, protocol draft, landing blueprint, and candidate project-file appendix are implementation-ready design text. They are not live project-root implementation until patched into the live ION project and verified.

## 2.4 Finalization Layer

This v3.1 layer gives the reader the operational map: terms, claims, files, blockers, and completion conditions.

# 3. Current Canon in One Page

ION is a governed maintained-work-surface architecture for AI-mediated collaboration.

Its current live center is:

```text
Maintained Work Surface
+ Front-Stage Council
+ Representational Integrity
+ Persona latency lanes
+ Expressive telemetry
+ Visual perception and interaction
+ Runtime claim receipts
+ non-production readiness boundaries
```

The governing product sentence is:

```text
ION turns AI collaboration into an inspectable maintained work surface.
```

The technical sentence is:

```text
ION converts user intent, AI work, artifacts, visual evidence, agent roles, claim classes, receipts, and continuation obligations into inspectable state that can be resumed, audited, repaired, and evolved.
```

The non-negotiable current rules are:

```text
1. ION remains NOT_PRODUCTION_READY.
2. V41 is the current supplied live project state described by this encyclopedia line.
3. V42 is a candidate next live branch, not implemented live in the project root by this encyclopedia artifact.
4. Persona is not all of ION.
5. Front-stage claims require Persona rendering state, Relay grounding, Steward/VZ verdict, emission permission, visibility level, and repair obligations.
6. No false certainty. No false uncertainty.
7. Rendered behavior is part of truth; source-code correctness is not product correctness.
8. Corrections are continuity events, not merely apologies.
9. Chat correction does not equal artifact correction.
10. Candidate project files are not live files until they are patched into the correct project root and verified.
```

---

# 4. Final Terms Glossary

## Agent activation

The controlled transition from a documented or candidate role into an executable support role with scope, authority, receipts, and kill conditions. V41 does not grant unrestricted agent activation.

## Artifact-target realignment

A repair class where work is moved from the wrong surface into the correct artifact root. In this encyclopedia line, the correction from canvas/side surface to Markdown encyclopedia packet is the canonical example.

## Candidate project file

Implementation-ready text for a future project-root patch. Candidate project files may be precise enough to copy into a project tree, but they are not live until actually patched, checked, tested, and receipted.

## Claim class

A V41 front-stage council classification for user-facing claims. The current ladder is C0 through C5: direct verified state, strong derived interpretation, proposal/design candidate, speculation/exploratory synthesis, unverified relay content, and forbidden representation.

## Conversational repair

A governed correction event that records what was wrong, what authority or evidence changed it, what artifacts were affected, what claim class moved, and what visible repair obligations remain.

## Front-Stage Council

The live user-facing governance model composed of Persona + Relay + Steward/VZ. Persona proposes or renders; Relay grounds; Steward/VZ authorizes or restricts; Persona emits under permission.

## Front-Stage Council Runtime Receipt

A V41 runtime-inspection object that classifies proposed user-facing claims before emission, including claim class, grounding, authority verdict, risk, permission, visibility, and repair obligations.

## Global graph canon

A still-unresolved production-gate requirement for global graph write, node, edge, region, conflict, migration, rollback, and authority semantics. The phrase must not be confused with the live branch number V36, which is already used in the V34–V41 self-mount lineage for the self-surface drift gate.

## Maintained Work Surface

The governed cognitive field in which user intent, operator pressure, AI synthesis, artifact evidence, protocols, tools, and emerging insight are kept mutually visible long enough to produce durable, inspectable progress.

## Persona

The user-facing rendering and intake surface. Persona may speak provisionally in low-risk lanes but may not claim to contain all of ION or independently possess all runtime truth.

## Production-gate namespace

A proposed namespace separating production requirements from branch numbers, for example `PG-GRAPH-01_GLOBAL_GRAPH_CANON` and `PG-AUDIT-01_ADVERSARIAL_PRODUCTION_AUDIT`.

## Relay

The grounding and translation boundary between user-facing expression and graph/project/runtime state. Relay must preserve provenance and avoid turning unverified context into truth.

## Steward/VZ

The authority/risk/classification side of the front-stage council. It determines whether a claim can be emitted, scoped, downgraded, blocked, or routed for repair.

## Visual Perception and Interaction Agent

The live project name for the bounded visual perception-and-interaction organ. It can be described as a support role for observing, diagnosing, comparing, navigating, testing, explaining, patch-requesting, and verifying authorized visual environments, but not as unrestricted visual automation.

# 8. Finalization Checklist

A finished encyclopedia edition should complete the following.

```yaml
required_for_final_documentary_edition:
  - remove or clearly quarantine inherited duplicate headings where historical body repeats current-state material
  - decide whether to keep historical v2.0 body inline or move it into historical appendix volume
  - settle final glossary terms and truename handling
  - verify all live-path claims against the latest supplied ION project root
  - reconcile production_readiness.py roadmap naming with the current live bootstrap lineage, or document the mismatch as intentionally unresolved
  - finalize production-gate namespace labels
  - create a finished edition manifest and claims ledger

required_for_project_implementation_claim:
  - patch V42 files into the live ION project root
  - run focused V42 tests
  - run existing focused V40/V41 production-readiness tests
  - run or explicitly bound the full project test suite
  - update project-root manifests and checksums
  - emit implementation receipts

required_for_production_ready_claim:
  - implement and verify global graph canon or equivalent production-gate namespace
  - implement source-summary rewrite authority or explicitly defer it
  - ratify agent activation authority
  - ratify production daemon authority
  - ratify product front-door authority
  - complete adversarial production audit
  - pass release-candidate verifier
```

---

# 9. Final Reader Warning

This encyclopedia is intentionally strong but not falsely final. It is now coherent enough to teach ION, rebuild large parts of ION’s conceptual stack, guide an implementation agent, and preserve the live V41/V42 direction. It is not allowed to erase its own blockers.

The correct reader stance is:

```text
Use v3.1 as the near-finished encyclopedia release candidate.
Use it to understand ION’s current live shape and next implementation path.
Do not treat it as proof that ION is production-ready.
```

---

# 10. v3.1 Settlement

```yaml
settled:
  - v3.0 is promoted from compiled near-finished draft to preserved master body
  - v3.1 adds final reader spine, glossary, claim ledger, protocol index, path index, and finalization checklist
  - the encyclopedia is now release-candidate-grade as documentation
  - the encyclopedia remains non-production-authoritative
  - V42 remains candidate text until project-root patch and verification

not_settled:
  - final editorial deduplication
  - V42 live project implementation
  - full-suite project verification
  - production-gate namespace implementation
  - production readiness
```


---

Instead, it establishes explicit precedence: the **Current-State Override**, **Live V41 Re-Anchor**, **V42 repair protocol**, **V42 landing blueprint**, and **V42 candidate project-file appendix** govern interpretation wherever older V2.0/V33/V35 language conflicts with the live V41/V42 state.

# 1. Executive Summary

ION is now best described as a governed maintained-work-surface architecture for AI-mediated collaboration. It turns user pressure, AI synthesis, artifacts, visual/rendered behavior, role boundaries, claim classes, receipts, and continuation obligations into maintained state rather than transient performance.

The core product sentence for this edition is:

```text
ION turns AI collaboration into an inspectable maintained work surface.
```

The stronger technical sentence is:

```text
ION is a governed maintained-work-surface runtime that converts user intent, AI work, artifacts, visual evidence, agent roles, claim classes, receipts, and continuation obligations into inspectable state that can be resumed, audited, repaired, and evolved.
```

The live V41 center is:

```text
Maintained Work Surface
+ Representational Integrity
+ Front-Stage Council
+ Live Persona Latency
+ Expressive Telemetry
+ Visual Perception and Interaction
+ Front-Stage Council Runtime Receipts
```

The next branch target is:

```text
V42_CONVERSATIONAL_RECEIPTS_AND_LIVE_REPAIR
```

V42 is not claimed as implemented in the project root by this encyclopedia. V42 exists here as seed, formal protocol draft, project-tree landing blueprint, and candidate project-file appendix.

---

# 2. Current Verdict

```yaml
encyclopedia_status: NEAR_FINISHED_RELEASE_CANDIDATE
project_status_described: V41_FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_RUNTIME_RECEIPTS
production_ready: false
current_product_center: Maintained Work Surface + Front-Stage Council Runtime Receipts
v42_status: candidate_design_and_landing_blueprint
visual_agent_live_name: Visual Perception and Interaction Agent
visual_agent_status: A3 doctrine/runtime-planning, not unrestricted automation
claim_receipt_status: V41 front-stage council runtime receipts present in live evidence packet
conversational_repair_status: V42 encyclopedia protocol and candidate files, not live project-root implementation
```

This document is ready to serve as a near-finished encyclopedia for continued project work, implementation planning, review, and external explanation. It is not final in the stronger sense because the live ION project still requires production-gate settlement, live V42 implementation, namespace repair, graph-canon authority, source-summary rewrite authority, adversarial audit, and production verification.

# 3. Precedence Rules for This Edition

Because the encyclopedia evolved over multiple packets, the v3.0 edition uses explicit precedence rules.

```yaml
highest_precedence:
  - this v3.0 front matter
  - Current-State Override
  - Live V41 Re-Anchor sections
  - V42 Conversational Receipts and Live Repair protocol sections
  - V42 Project-Tree Landing Blueprint
  - V42 Candidate Project Files Appendix

historical_or_lineage_precedence:
  - v2.0 release candidate body
  - V10-V33 runtime lineage chapters
  - V34/V35 demo-to-production primitive split material
  - early V36 global graph canon seed language

interpretation_rule:
  - older branch-number roadmap language remains historically useful
  - older branch-number roadmap language must not override the live V41/V42 branch line
  - production-gate requirements must be understood through the namespace map below
```

The most important correction is the branch/gate separation:

```text
Live branch versions are not identical to production-gate identifiers.
```

Older text that says “V36 Global Graph Canon” should now be read as a production-gate requirement, not as the current live branch number. In the current live self-mount/front-stage branch line, V36 is already used for `SELF_SURFACE_DRIFT_GATE`. Therefore production gates need their own namespace.

```text
v2.0 — consolidated encyclopedia packet through V35 demo-to-production primitive split
v2.1 — live V41 re-anchor
v2.2 — V42 conversational repair seed
```

```text

V34 — GPT-5.5 self-mount delegation lock
V35 — runtime identity envelope lock
V36 — self-surface drift gate lock
V37 — agent succession packet lock
V38 — self-mount graph integration lock
V39 — front-door self-mount binding lock
V40 — maintained work surface and persona-system canon lock
V41 — front-stage council runtime receipts lock
V42 — conversational receipts and live repair, proposed next live branch
```

## 4.3 Production-gate namespace

```text
PG-GRAPH-01      — Global Graph Canon
PG-SUMMARY-01    — Source Summary Rewrite Proposal Authority
PG-SUMMARY-02    — Source Summary Rewrite Review and Bounded Commit Authority
PG-AGENT-01      — Agent Activation Authority

```

## 4.4 Demo/release-candidate milestones

```text
V10-V32 — bounded evented graph, summary-refresh demo, replay, doctoring, certification, evidence bundle, release-candidate verifier lineage
```

The encyclopedia should not collapse these namespaces. Doing so would recreate exactly the kind of semantic drift ION exists to prevent.

# 6. Non-Negotiable Current Canon Rules

```text
1. ION turns collaboration itself into infrastructure.

2. The maintained work surface is the current product-level center of ION.

3. The user-facing ION presence is produced by a front-stage council: Persona + Relay + Steward/VZ.

4. A user-facing claim does not become true because the Persona sounds confident.

5. No false certainty. No false uncertainty.

6. Front-stage council receipts classify claims into C0 through C5 and produce emission permissions, visibility levels, and repair obligations.

7. Persona expression may be fast only in low-risk provisional lanes.

8. Corrections are continuity events, not merely apologies.

9. Chat correction does not equal artifact correction.

10. Rendered behavior is part of truth; source-code correctness is not product correctness.

11. The live project name for the visual agent is Visual Perception and Interaction Agent.

12. Visual/computer-use authority remains bounded; unrestricted visual automation is forbidden.

13. V42 candidate project files in this encyclopedia are not live project-root files until explicitly patched into the project root and verified.

14. V41 remains non-production-authoritative.
```

---

# 7. Open Finalization Requirements

This v3.0 edition is near-finished. It becomes a stronger final encyclopedia only after these are handled:

```yaml
required_for_final_encyclopedia:
  - global edit pass to remove or mark all stale V36-as-branch language
  - final namespace repair across all old roadmap tables
  - final glossary and path index
  - project-root V42 implementation or explicit deferral
  - live project verification after V42 patch, if patched
  - full-suite test result or explicit non-claim
  - checksum and manifest verification for final artifact
  - reviewer pass for contradictions between v2.0 body and V41/V42 override
```

Required for production-ready ION remains much larger:

```yaml
required_for_production_ready_ion:
  - PG-GRAPH-01 global graph canon
  - PG-SUMMARY source-summary rewrite authority
  - PG-AGENT and PG-SUBAGENT activation authority
  - PG-DAEMON production daemon runtime loop
  - PG-FRONTDOOR production front-door authority
  - PG-AUDIT adversarial production audit
  - PG-RELEASE production release candidate
  - PG-VERIFY production verifier
```

# Current-State Override

The sections immediately following this heading supersede any older v2.0 statements that describe `V34_A3_SURFACE_RATIFICATION_PASS` as the next live move, describe `V36_GLOBAL_GRAPH_CANON` as the next live branch number, or describe the visual agent as missing from the live tree.

Where the older body says `V36_GLOBAL_GRAPH_CANON`, read that as an unresolved **production-gate requirement** unless a later ratified branch explicitly renames or re-promotes it. The current live V36 branch in the supplied project root is `V36_SELF_SURFACE_DRIFT_GATE_LOCK`.

Where the older body says `V40_SUBAGENT_FAN_OUT_FAN_IN_RUNTIME` or `V41_DAEMON_RUNTIME_LOOP` as future branch numbers, read those as older production-gate roadmap labels requiring namespace repair. The current live V40/V41 branch surfaces are:

```text
V40_MAINTAINED_WORK_SURFACE_AND_PERSONA_SYSTEM_LOCK
V41_FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_RUNTIME_RECEIPTS_LOCK
```


---

# 1. Current Live State

The current supplied ION project evidence is no longer merely the V33/V35 readiness line described by v2.0. It is now:

```text
V41_FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_RUNTIME_RECEIPTS
```

The live V41 project packet contains a V40 maintained-work-surface/persona-system canon package and a V41 front-stage-council runtime-receipt package. The encyclopedia must therefore stop describing `V34_A3_SURFACE_RATIFICATION_PASS` as the next live project move. That was correct for the v2.0 packet at the time of its assembly; it is no longer the live state after the V41 packet.

Correct current state:

```yaml
current_live_project_packet: V41_FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_RUNTIME_RECEIPTS
current_encyclopedia_update: v2.1_live_v41
production_ready: false
production_authority: false
global_graph_canon_authority: false
source_summary_rewrite_authority: false
unrestricted_agent_activation_authority: false
unrestricted_visual_automation_authority: false
front_stage_council_runtime_receipts: present
maintained_work_surface_canon: present
visual_perception_and_interaction_agent_protocol: present
```

The key product-level shift is:

```text
ION is now best described as a governed maintained-work-surface runtime for AI-mediated collaboration.
```

The older graph-operating-system sentence remains true as a substrate description, but the live V41 product center is now the maintained work surface plus the front-stage council.

---

# 2. Corrected Product Thesis

The v2.0 product thesis was:

```text
ION lets AI agents remember, coordinate, and evolve complex work by turning context into a governed living graph.
```

That remains valid, but v2.1 must now lead with the stronger live V41 formulation:

```text
ION turns AI collaboration into an inspectable maintained work surface.
```

Expanded form:

```text
ION is a governed maintained-work-surface runtime that converts user intent, AI synthesis, artifact evidence, visual/rendered behavior, agent roles, claim classes, receipts, and continuation obligations into inspectable state that can be resumed, audited, repaired, and evolved.
```

The live maintained-work-surface doctrine defines the surface as:

```text
The governed cognitive field in which user intent, operator pressure, AI synthesis, artifact evidence, protocols, tools, and emerging insight are kept mutually visible long enough to produce durable, inspectable progress.
```

The live universal workflow grammar is:

```text
pressure -> synthesis -> evidence -> recognition -> formalization -> receipt -> continuation
```

The live canon sentence is:

```text
ION turns collaboration itself into infrastructure.
```

This is now the encyclopedia’s current center.

---

# 3. Corrected Lineage

The v2.0 encyclopedia carried a production-roadmap sequence that treated V34–V45 as future production gates. The V41 project packet shows that the live branch has continued through a different self-mount/front-stage lineage.

The V41 packet contains the following bootstrap locks:

```text
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V32_CERTIFIED_DEMO_BASELINE_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V34_GPT55_SELF_MOUNT_DELEGATION_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V35_RUNTIME_IDENTITY_ENVELOPE_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V36_SELF_SURFACE_DRIFT_GATE_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V37_AGENT_SUCCESSION_PACKET_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V38_SELF_MOUNT_GRAPH_INTEGRATION_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V39_FRONT_DOOR_SELF_MOUNT_BINDING_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V40_MAINTAINED_WORK_SURFACE_AND_PERSONA_SYSTEM_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V41_FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_RUNTIME_RECEIPTS_LOCK.md
```

Corrected live lineage:

```text
V32 — certified demo baseline
V34 — GPT-5.5 self-mount delegation lock
V35 — runtime identity envelope lock
V36 — self-surface drift gate lock
V37 — agent succession packet lock
V38 — self-mount graph integration lock
V39 — front-door self-mount binding lock
V40 — maintained work surface and persona-system canon lock
V41 — front-stage council runtime receipts lock
```

Important boundary:

```text
There is no V33 bootstrap lock in the current V41 packet’s 00_BOOTSTRAP set.
```

V33 remains meaningful as an earlier production-readiness framing in the encyclopedia/project history, but the current live V41 lock sequence does not include a V33 bootstrap lock. The encyclopedia must not invent one.

# 4. Production-Gate Roadmap vs Live Branch Numbering

The V41 project still includes a `production_readiness.py` module. Focused tests confirm it returns `NOT_PRODUCTION_READY`. However, its internal `next_sequence` still carries the older production-gate numbering:

```text
V35_DEMO_PRODUCTION_PRIMITIVE_SPLIT
V36_GLOBAL_GRAPH_CANON_PROTOCOL_AND_REGISTRY
V37_SOURCE_SUMMARY_REWRITE_PROPOSAL_ONLY
V38_SOURCE_SUMMARY_REWRITE_REVIEW_AND_BOUNDED_COMMIT
V39_AGENT_ACTIVATION_AUTHORITY_PROTOCOL
V40_SUBAGENT_FAN_OUT_FAN_IN_RUNTIME
V41_DAEMON_RUNTIME_LOOP
V42_PRODUCTION_FRONT_DOOR_CLI_API
V43_ADVERSARIAL_PRODUCTION_AUDIT
```

That sequence is not identical to the live V34–V41 bootstrap lineage. This is a roadmap-lineage drift, not a production-safety failure, because the production verdict remains blocked.

Correct classification:

```yaml
drift_id: production_readiness_next_sequence_vs_live_bootstrap_lineage_mismatch
kind: roadmap_lineage_staleness
severity: medium
safe_status_preserved: true
reason_safe: production_readiness.py still returns NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
production_impact: blocks_using_old_next_sequence_as_current_live_branch_map
repair:
  - distinguish production-gate roadmap from live self-mount/front-stage branch numbering
  - namespace production gates separately from branch versions
  - preserve NOT_PRODUCTION_READY until formal ratification
```

Recommended namespace repair:

```text
PG-GRAPH-01_GLOBAL_GRAPH_CANON
PG-SUMMARY-01_SOURCE_SUMMARY_REWRITE_AUTHORITY
PG-AGENT-01_AGENT_ACTIVATION_AUTHORITY
PG-DAEMON-01_PRODUCTION_DAEMON_AUTHORITY
PG-FRONTDOOR-01_PRODUCT_FRONT_DOOR_AUTHORITY
PG-AUDIT-01_ADVERSARIAL_PRODUCTION_AUDIT
```

This prevents branch-version numbers from colliding with production-gate numbers.

# 6. V41 Actually Landed: Front-Stage Council Runtime Receipts

The V41 front-stage-council receipt package is present in the live project tree.

Required V41 surfaces include:

```text
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V41_FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_RUNTIME_RECEIPTS_LOCK.md
ION/02_architecture/FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_RUNTIME_RECEIPT_PROTOCOL.md
ION/03_registry/front_stage_council_receipt.schema.json
ION/03_registry/front_stage_council_runtime_policy.yaml
ION/04_packages/kernel/front_stage_council_receipt.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_front_stage_council_receipt.py
```

The V41 protocol converts front-stage council doctrine into a runtime receipt object. It records whether a proposed user-facing claim has:

```text
1. Persona composition/rendering state;
2. Relay grounding/provenance state;
3. Steward/VZ claim-class and risk verdict;
4. user-facing emission permission;
5. required visibility level;
6. repair/retraction obligations if the claim cannot be emitted cleanly.
```

The live claim classes are:

```text
C0 — direct verified state
C1 — strong derived interpretation
C2 — proposal or design candidate
C3 — speculation or exploratory synthesis
C4 — unverified relay content
C5 — forbidden representation
```

The live emission permissions are:

```text
MAY_EMIT_DIRECTLY
MAY_EMIT_WITH_SCOPE
MAY_EMIT_AS_PROPOSAL
MAY_EMIT_AS_SPECULATION
MAY_BACKCHANNEL_ONLY
BLOCKED_REQUIRES_REPAIR
BLOCKED_FORBIDDEN_REPRESENTATION
```

The live visibility levels are:

```text
QUIET
EXPANDABLE
MANDATORY
BLOCKING
```

Example V41 receipt generated during this pass:

```yaml
version: V41_FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_RUNTIME_RECEIPTS
claim_class: C0
persona_state: RENDER_READY
relay_state: GROUNDED
steward_verdict: APPROVED
risk_level: LOW
emission_permission: MAY_EMIT_DIRECTLY
visibility_level: EXPANDABLE
repair_required: false
production_authority: false
```

This is one of the strongest live ION advances. ION no longer merely says the Persona should avoid overclaim. It now has a receipt object for classifying user-facing claim emission.

---

# 7. Corrected Front-Stage Model

The v2.0 encyclopedia’s front-door model remains structurally useful, but v2.1 must describe the current live model as:

```text
Front-Stage Council = Persona + Relay + Steward/VZ
```

Council law:

```text
Persona proposes or renders.
Relay grounds.
Steward/VZ authorizes.
Persona emits.
```

The user experiences one coherent presence, but the system must preserve the distinction between:

```text
relationship/expression,
context transport/provenance/freshness,
authority/risk/claim class/work legitimacy.
```

Core anti-theatre law:

```text
A multi-agent output is not trustworthy because it sounds collaborative.
It is trustworthy only when council roles are explicit, claim class is controlled, and the evidence path is recoverable.
```

This should govern all future encyclopedia language about ION’s user-facing agentic presence.

---

# 8. Representational Integrity and Provisional Speech

The V41 packet includes V40 doctrine for representational integrity, persona context budgets, expressive telemetry, and provisional utterance.

The corrected encyclopedia rule is:

```text
No false certainty. No false uncertainty.
```

Verified truth should not be weakened merely to sound modest. Unverified claims must not be strengthened merely to sound coherent.

The live persona latency lanes are:

```text
L0 — backchannel
L1 — conversational provisional
L2 — checked response
L3 — ratified answer
L4 — formal artifact
```

The Persona may emit low-risk provisional speech in L0/L1 lanes, but high-impact or durable claims require stronger checking, receipt, or repair.

Never-provisional classes include:

```text
production authority
destructive actions
security-sensitive actions
legal/medical/financial high-stakes guidance
credential use
identity/personhood claims
file/test proof claims
```

This allows ION to be conversationally alive without allowing fluent theatre to become authority.

---

# 9. Expressive Telemetry

The V41 packet includes expressive telemetry and affect-integrity doctrine. The encyclopedia should treat expression as governed representational telemetry, not as a claim of human emotion.

Valid expressive signals may include:

```text
tone
pacing
warmth
hesitation
seriousness
formality
curiosity
celebration
restraint
future avatar gestures
```

They may represent:

```text
confidence
uncertainty
drift
risk
verification
momentum
care
```

They must not fabricate:

```text
inner suffering
dependency
romance
coercive intimacy
false personhood
false user obligation
```

The canon sentence is:

```text
Emotion is not the mask. Emotion is the dashboard.
```

In encyclopedia terms, this means affect is an interface channel for system-state telemetry, not a claim that the system is human.

---

# 10. Visual Perception and Interaction Agent: Live Name and Corrected Status

The v2.1 discussion draft previously used `Visual Operator` as a candidate name. The live project already contains the actual current surface:

```text
ION/02_architecture/VISUAL_PERCEPTION_AND_INTERACTION_AGENT_PROTOCOL.md
ION/03_registry/visual_perception_agent_policy.yaml
```

Corrected handling:

```yaml
previous_discussion_name: Visual Operator
live_project_name: Visual Perception and Interaction Agent
status: A3_DOCTRINE_AND_RUNTIME_PLANNING
production_authority: false
unrestricted_control_authority: false
```

The live visual-agent purpose is:

```text
ION shall maintain a bounded visual perception-and-interaction organ capable of inspecting, diagnosing, navigating, and explaining authorized visual environments.
```

The live product rule is:

```text
Rendered behavior is part of truth. Source-code correctness is not product correctness.
```

Live modes:

```text
OBSERVE
DIAGNOSE
COMPARE
NAVIGATE
TEST
EXPLAIN
PATCH_REQUEST
VERIFY
```

Allowed initial scope:

```text
screenshot_analysis
dom_read_inspection
local_dev_ui_navigation
before_after_visual_receipts
```

Forbidden without explicit authorization:

```text
destructive_action
credential_sensitive_action
purchase_or_submission
deletion_or_irreversible_mutation
arbitrary_account_operation
```

Therefore the earlier Visual Operator authority ladder should be retained only as candidate elaboration under the live Visual Perception and Interaction Agent name. It should not be treated as a separate role unless a later truename review explicitly splits the organ.

---

# 11. Visual Evidence Must Become Maintained Work-Surface Evidence

The live visual-agent surface should be integrated into the maintained-work-surface loop:

```text
Visual Agent OBSERVE / DIAGNOSE / COMPARE / VERIFY
→ visual evidence packet
→ front-stage council receipt if user-facing
→ maintained work surface continuation
→ PATCH_REQUEST if implementation is needed
→ implementation/change receipt if authorized
→ post-patch VERIFY
→ before/after visual receipt
```

The candidate packet classes from the prior evolution pass remain valuable, but they should now be labeled as candidate elaborations:

```yaml
visual_observation_packet: candidate template extension
visual_diagnosis_packet: candidate template extension
visual_action_proposal_packet: candidate template extension
visual_comparison_packet: candidate template extension
visual_operation_receipt: candidate template extension
```

The governing rule remains:

```text
Observation may enter as witness.
Action must enter as proposal.
Mutation requires authority.
Completion requires receipt.
```

```text
front-stage council receipts classify claim emission but do not make claims true by themselves.
```

The key distinction:

```text
V41 adds a runtime object for claim-emission governance.
V41 does not make all claims true.
```

---

# 14. Updated Canon Rules

This v2.1 update adds the following corrected canon rules:

```text
1. ION turns collaboration itself into infrastructure.

2. The maintained work surface is the current product-level center of ION.

3. The user-facing ION presence is governed by a front-stage council: Persona + Relay + Steward/VZ.

4. Persona expression is allowed to be fast only in low-risk provisional lanes.

5. High-impact user-facing claims require claim-class control, grounding/provenance, authority/risk verdict, and emission permission.

6. Front-stage council receipts classify claims into C0 through C5 and produce emission permissions, visibility levels, and repair obligations.

7. A statement does not become ION truth because the Persona sounds confident.

8. No false certainty; no false uncertainty.

9. Expressive telemetry may render system state, but must not fabricate human emotion or coercive intimacy.

10. Rendered behavior is part of truth; source-code correctness is not product correctness.

11. The Visual Perception and Interaction Agent is live as an A3 doctrine/runtime-planning surface, not unrestricted automation.

12. V41 remains non-production-authoritative.
```

---

# 17. Closing Principle

```text
ION makes AI collaboration compound by turning work, evidence, expression, visual behavior, agent roles, claims, receipts, and continuation pressure into maintained state instead of transient performance.
```

This is the current live encyclopedia center.

# Executive Summary

[PROVISIONAL] ION is a living context graph operating system for AI work. It lets agents remember, coordinate, and evolve complex projects by turning files, templates, packets, receipts, roles, summaries, workflows, releases, and reviews into governed graph objects.

The current v2.0 encyclopedia posture is deliberately conservative:

```text
V10 = first bounded evented-template graph commit milestone
V32 = certified demo baseline
V33 = production-readiness frame
current production verdict = NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
```

[RUNTIME-PROVEN] The V10–V32 lineage proves that ION can execute and verify a bounded release-demo path. [A3-PROPOSAL] V33 defines the production-readiness frame and names the production gates. [PRODUCTION-GATED] It does not close those gates.

This release candidate is a documentation release candidate for the encyclopedia. It is not an ION production release.

| Production readiness | `NOT_PRODUCTION_READY` |
| V10 | Runtime milestone, not current endpoint |
| V32 | Certified demo baseline, not production release |
| V33 | Production-readiness frame, not production readiness itself |
| Global graph canon | Blocked until V36 |
| Source-summary rewrite authority | Blocked until V37–V38 |
| Agent/subagent activation authority | Blocked until V39–V40 |
| Production daemon authority | Blocked until V41 |
| Production front-door product surface | Blocked until V42 |
| Adversarial production audit | Blocked until V43 |
| Production release candidate | Blocked until V44 |
| Production verifier | Blocked until V45 |
| Codex live authority | Historical-only; not current orchestrator |
| Current orchestration truename | Steward |
| Front-door chain | Persona Interface → Relay → Steward |

# Volume 0 — Authority, Source, and How to Read

## 1. Opening Disclosure

This document is the opening authority frame for the ION Production Encyclopedia v2.0.

It exists because the current ION encyclopedia reached the correct conceptual center, but its runtime posture must now be updated. The existing encyclopedia correctly identifies ION as a living context graph operated by lawful agents through templates. It correctly recognizes that a completed template-file is not merely a document, but a template-instantiated graph object capable of creating lawful event pressure. It correctly preserves the distinction between Persona Interface, Relay, and Steward. It correctly warns against collapsing smooth prose, runtime proof, proposal, doctrine, and authority into one undifferentiated claim.

However, the current encyclopedia’s runtime frame still centers V10 as the current evented-template graph implementation. That was an important runtime milestone, but the live project lineage has advanced. The production encyclopedia must now treat V10 as the first bounded evented-template graph commit milestone, while treating V32 as the certified demo baseline and V33 as the current production-readiness posture.

This document does **not** claim ION is production-ready.

It claims something narrower and stronger:

```text
ION has recovered its correct root invariant.
ION has a certified and independently verifiable release-demo spine.
ION has a production-readiness charter.
ION has an explicit ratification path.
ION is not production-ready until the remaining production gates pass.
```

That distinction is the purpose of this preface.

---

## 2. The Core Product Sentence

ION lets AI agents remember, coordinate, and evolve complex work by turning context into a governed living graph.

This is the shortest product form. It is useful because it avoids false complexity while preserving the root substrate:

```text
AI agents
complex work
context
governed living graph
```

A longer product form:

```text
ION is a living context graph operating system for AI work: it turns files, agents, templates, packets, receipts, registries, runtime sessions, release artifacts, and front-door interactions into lawful graph objects whose evolution can be validated, reviewed, certified, verified, resumed, and carried across model, chat, IDE, daemon, API, and archive boundaries.
```

This production encyclopedia must serve both sentences. It must be understandable at product altitude and exact at builder altitude.

---

## 3. Why This Encyclopedia Exists

ION is too large and too interdependent to be represented by a normal README, architecture note, or project summary.

ION requires an encyclopedia because it is simultaneously:

```text
a doctrine of governed AI work
a filesystem law model
a context graph substrate
an evented template runtime
a front-door product architecture
a release-demo spine
a certification/evidence system
a future production runtime
a recovery and continuity protocol
```

A normal document can explain one of these. The production encyclopedia must explain how all of them remain one system without collapsing their authority levels.

The encyclopedia must answer:

```text
What is ION?
What has ION proven?
What remains provisional?
What is demo-only?
What is production-gated?
What can mutate what?
What can only propose?
What can be reviewed?
What can be committed?
What can be verified?
What must never be claimed yet?
```

---

## 4. Current Production Posture

The current production posture is intentionally conservative.

```yaml
ion_current_posture:
  certified_demo_baseline: V32
  production_readiness_frame: V33
  production_verdict: NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
  release_demo_status: certified_and_verified
  next_lawful_production_gate: V34_A3_SURFACE_RATIFICATION_PASS
```

## 4.1 V32 means certified demo baseline

V32 proves that the release-demo capsule can be independently verified. It checks that an existing release-candidate capsule is structurally intact, checksum-consistent, certified, and evidence-backed.

V32 does not mean ION is production-ready.

## 4.2 V33 means production-readiness frame

V33 establishes the production-readiness charter, gap register, and ratification matrix frame.

V33 does not close the production gaps. It names them.

## 4.3 Current verdict

```text
NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
```

This is not a failure. It is a lawful boundary.

A system this complex should not be called production-ready merely because one demo path is certified. Production readiness requires ratified authority, generalized primitives, graph canon, source-summary rewrite authority, agent activation law, daemon safety, and adversarial audit.

---

## 5. Source Authority Ledger

The encyclopedia must distinguish sources by authority and function.

## 5.1 Primary conceptual source

```text
ION_Constitutional_Current_Evented_Living_Context_Graph_Runtime_Edition_v1_1.md
```

### Status

```text
strongest current conceptual encyclopedia source
accurate root invariant
runtime posture stale after V32/V33
```

### Preserved claims

```text
ION is a living context graph operated by lawful agents through templates.
Files can become template-instantiated graph objects.
Completed template files can create lawful event pressure.
Persona Interface, Relay, and Steward are distinct.
Codex is historical-only in the current root.
V10 proves a bounded evented-template graph commit path.
```

### Required correction

```text
V10 must become runtime milestone, not current endpoint.
V32 must become certified demo baseline.
V33 must become current production-readiness frame.
```

## 5.2 Certified demo baseline source

```text
V32_SUMMARY_REFRESH_DEMO_RELEASE_CANDIDATE_VERIFIER
```

### Status

```text
certified release-demo baseline
independent release-candidate verification infrastructure
not production completion
```

### Use in encyclopedia

```text
Use V32 to anchor what has been certified and verified.
Do not use V32 as evidence of full production readiness.
```

## 5.3 Production-readiness frame source

```text
V33_PRODUCTION_READINESS_CHARTER_AND_RATIFICATION_MATRIX
```

### Status

```text
current production-readiness posture
production verdict = NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
next lawful move = V34_A3_SURFACE_RATIFICATION_PASS
```

### Use in encyclopedia

```text
Use V33 to define production gates, gaps, and ratification discipline.
Do not use V33 to claim those gates are closed.
```

## 5.4 Runtime lineage sources

| Source | Meaning | Encyclopedia posture |
|---|---|---|
| V10 | first bounded evented-template graph commit | runtime milestone |
| V17 | evented runtime plus front-door demo spine | integration milestone |
| V26 | full summary-refresh bounded commit demo | demo-proven workflow path |
| V27 | replay CLI | replay infrastructure |
| V28 | replay doctor | operator validation infrastructure |
| V29 | certification gate | certification infrastructure |
| V30 | evidence bundle | evidence packaging infrastructure |
| V31 | release-candidate capsule | release handoff infrastructure |
| V32 | release-candidate verifier | certified demo baseline |
| V33 | production-readiness charter | production-readiness frame |

## 5.5 Historical sources

Historical ION, Aether, AIMOS, and donor-line documents are valuable as lineage and recovery evidence.

They may be used to recover:

```text
lost doctrine
original invariants
semantic ancestry
template concepts
agent role ancestry
governance concepts
```

They may not automatically override:

```text
current root names
current role truename
V32 certified demo baseline
V33 production-readiness posture
ratification matrix decisions
```

## 5.6 Runtime artifact hierarchy

When sources conflict, use this order:

```text
1. ratified constitutional law
2. enacted runtime code and tests
3. verified release-candidate artifacts
4. production-readiness reports
5. current encyclopedia synthesis
6. historical/donor-line encyclopedia synthesis
7. conversational explanation
```

This hierarchy prevents beautiful prose from outranking enacted evidence.

---

## 6. Claims Ledger

The production encyclopedia must not contain unmarked major claims. Each major claim should be tagged.

## 6.1 Claim tags

| Tag | Meaning |
|---|---|
| `[A1-CROWN]` | crown constitutional law |
| `[A2-GOVERNANCE]` | ratified production governance |
| `[A3-PROPOSAL]` | operational proposal or current-phase surface |
| `[A4-DEMO]` | demo/evidence/release-demo surface |
| `[RUNTIME-PROVEN]` | proven by enacted code/tests/smoke |
| `[DEMO-PROVEN]` | proven only in bounded release-demo path |
| `[PRODUCTION-GATED]` | required for production but not yet complete |
| `[PROVISIONAL]` | strong but not yet ratified |
| `[HISTORICAL-ONLY]` | lineage evidence only |
| `[DEPRECATED]` | must not be used in new authority paths |
| `[ASPIRATIONAL]` | future intended direction |

## 6.2 Examples

```text
[PROVISIONAL] ION is a living context graph operated by lawful agents through templates.
[RUNTIME-PROVEN] V32 can verify an existing release-candidate capsule.
[DEMO-PROVEN] The summary-refresh path can run through bounded graph-state commit.
[PRODUCTION-GATED] ION must define global graph canon before production graph authority.
[HISTORICAL-ONLY] Codex is historical carrier/chassis lineage, not the current orchestration truename.
```

## 6.3 Forbidden untagged claims

The following may not appear without clear status tags:

```text
ION is production-ready.
ION has global graph canon.
ION can safely rewrite source summaries.
ION can autonomously activate arbitrary subagents.
ION has production daemon safety.
All A3 surfaces are ratified.
The summary-refresh demo runner is a production-general workflow runner.
```

---

## 7. Non-Overclaim Boundaries

The production encyclopedia must preserve these boundaries.

## 7.1 Certified demo is not production

A certified demo path proves that the architecture can enact a bounded chain. It does not prove the entire system can run safely under all production conditions.

## 7.2 Bounded graph-state commit is not global graph canon

The V26 path commits to bounded evented-template graph state. It does not prove global graph canon.

## 7.3 Source summary is not yet safely mutable

ION’s future value depends on self-documenting and self-updating summaries, but direct source-summary rewrite is dangerous. Production source-summary rewrite requires proposal, diff, provenance, review, bounded commit, and rollback.

## 7.4 Agent/subagent theory is not yet activation authority

The architecture needs domain managers, specialist agents, and contextual node workers. But production agent activation requires leases, context packages, permissions, receipts, kill switches, and fan-in law.

## 7.5 Release-candidate verification is not constitutional ratification

V32 verifies the release-demo capsule. It does not ratify provisional A3 surfaces into production governance.

---

## 8. Reader Instructions

## 8.1 For human readers

Read this encyclopedia as a layered authority document.

Do not ask only:

```text
Does this sound coherent?
```

Ask:

```text
What authority class is this claim?
What evidence supports it?
Is it doctrine, runtime proof, demo proof, proposal, or production law?
What can mutate what?
What remains blocked?
```

## 8.2 For AI builder agents

Treat this encyclopedia as a context and reconstruction guide, not as automatic mutation authority.

You may use it to:

```text
understand ION
locate surfaces
plan implementation
generate scaffold drafts
create proposal packets
create ratification matrices
```

You may not use it to:

```text
rewrite canonical law without review
claim production readiness
promote provisional surfaces
activate agents
rewrite source summaries
mutate global graph canon
```

## 8.3 For reviewer agents

Treat the encyclopedia as a claims map.

Review questions:

```text
Is each major claim tagged?
Is V10 framed as milestone rather than current endpoint?
Is V32 framed as certified demo baseline?
Is V33 framed as NOT_PRODUCTION_READY?
Are demo-only surfaces kept separate from production primitives?
Are historical roles prevented from reentering live authority?
```

---

## 9. Preface for the Full v2.0 Encyclopedia

The following text should become the opening preface of the full production encyclopedia.

---

## Preface

ION is a living context graph operating system for AI work.

It exists because ordinary AI workflows lose continuity, confuse memory with authority, collapse explanation into action, and let agents operate without enough durable context, proof, or review. ION answers that problem by turning work itself into a governed graph: files, templates, packets, receipts, agents, registries, summaries, questions, runtime sessions, and release artifacts become lawful graph objects whose evolution can be validated, reviewed, certified, verified, resumed, and carried across systems.

The simplest product explanation is this:

```text
ION lets AI agents remember, coordinate, and evolve complex work by turning context into a governed living graph.
```

The deeper technical explanation is that ION is a continuity substrate. It does not merely store information for later retrieval. It structures work at the moment of creation so future agents can inherit the correct context, authority, evidence, and next action. In ION, the file is not just a file. A lawful file is a template-instantiated graph object. A completed file can create event pressure. Event pressure can create reactions. Reactions can create projections, proposals, reviews, bounded commits, receipts, evidence bundles, release candidates, and verifications.

This encyclopedia is the production-readiness edition. It preserves the recovered root invariant of the current ION encyclopedia while updating the runtime posture to the V33 baseline.

The current state is precise:

```text
V32 is the certified demo baseline.
V33 is the production-readiness frame.
ION is not yet production-ready.
```

This distinction matters. A lesser document would call the certified demo a finished product. ION must not do that. ION’s purpose is lawful continuity, not premature triumph. Therefore this encyclopedia separates what is proven, what is demo-proven, what is provisional, what is historical, and what remains production-gated.

The certified release-demo spine proves that ION can run a bounded chain from front-door intake through template, event, reaction, projection, proposal, review, bounded commit, evidence, release candidate, and verification. That is a major result. It does not yet prove global graph canon, source-summary rewrite authority, production agent activation, daemon production safety, or full adversarial audit completion.

The production path is now explicit. The next lawful production gate is the A3 surface ratification pass. After that, ION must split demo surfaces from production primitives, ratify graph canon, govern source-summary rewrite, define agent and subagent activation authority, harden the daemon loop, productize the front door, and pass adversarial audit.

This encyclopedia exists so that future builders do not need to rediscover the system by accident. It is meant to be complete enough that an AI builder can reconstruct ION’s doctrine, runtime spine, certified demo path, production-readiness gates, and remaining ratification sequence without hidden oral context.

It is also meant to be honest.

ION is no longer merely an idea. It has a certified demo baseline.

ION is not yet production-ready. It has the gate that says what production-ready means.

That is the correct foundation.

---

```yaml
source_ledger_summary:

    status: strongest_current_conceptual_source

    name: V33_PRODUCTION_READINESS_CHARTER_AND_RATIFICATION_MATRIX
    status: current_production_readiness_frame
    production_verdict: NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
  next_gate:
    name: V34_A3_SURFACE_RATIFICATION_PASS
```

# Volume I — Runtime Lineage V10–V33

## 1. Why Runtime Lineage Matters

ION cannot be explained correctly if its runtime lineage is flattened.

A normal software history can say:

```text
version X added feature Y.
```

ION requires a stricter history:

```text
version X proved claim Y under boundary Z, without proving claims A, B, or C.
```

This matters because ION’s central risk is not failure to invent concepts. Its central risk is **claim laundering**: a concept becomes plausible, then a demo proves a narrow path, then a later document accidentally treats that narrow proof as full production authority.

The production encyclopedia must therefore track:

```text
what each runtime version proved
what evidence supported the proof
what authority class the proof has
what the version explicitly did not prove
what production gap remained after the version
```

The lineage from V10 to V33 is the first clean demonstration of this discipline. It begins with the first bounded evented-template graph commit and ends, for now, with a production-readiness charter that explicitly says ION is not production-ready.

That is correct.

---

## 2. Lineage Summary

```text
V10  -> first bounded evented-template graph commit
V17  -> evented runtime + front-door demo spine
V26  -> complete summary-refresh bounded commit demo
V27  -> replay CLI
V28  -> replay doctor
V29  -> certification gate
V30  -> evidence bundle
V31  -> release-candidate capsule
V32  -> release-candidate verifier
V33  -> production-readiness charter and ratification matrix
```

Short form:

```text
event -> front door -> bounded commit -> replay -> doctor -> certification -> evidence -> release candidate -> verifier -> production readiness gate
```

This lineage proves that ION has moved beyond doctrine into a bounded, certifiable runtime path.

It does not prove full production readiness.

---

## 3. V10 — First Bounded Evented-Template Graph Commit

**Lineage status:** runtime milestone  
**Claim class:** `[RUNTIME-PROVEN]` within bounded evented-template graph path  
**Production status:** source of production primitive, not production endpoint

## 3.1 What V10 proved

V10 proved that a completed template-instantiated file can pass through an evented chain:

```text
completed template file
→ completion event
→ reaction selection
→ index projection
→ proposal
→ review
→ bounded graph commit
```

This was the first hard runtime proof that ION files could behave as graph objects rather than inert documents.

## 3.2 Why V10 matters

V10 is the first mechanical enactment of the core doctrine:

```text
A lawful file is not just a file.
A lawful file can become a graph event surface.
```

Without V10, the living context graph would remain mostly conceptual. With V10, ION had its first bounded runtime proof.

## 3.3 What V10 did not prove

V10 did not prove:

```text
front-door product operation
release-demo certification
global graph canon
source-summary rewrite authority
production daemon safety
agent/subagent activation authority
full production readiness
```

## 3.4 Encyclopedia correction

The current encyclopedia’s V10-centered runtime frame must be corrected.

Correct production encyclopedia language:

```text
V10 was the first bounded evented-template graph commit milestone.
```

Incorrect language:

```text
V10 is the current final runtime posture.
```

---

## 4. V17 — Evented Runtime + Front-Door Demo Spine

**Lineage status:** integration milestone  
**Claim class:** `[RUNTIME-PROVEN]` / `[DEMO-PROVEN]`  
**Production status:** front-door integration source, not full product front door

## 4.1 What V17 added

V17 connected the evented template runtime to the product-facing front-door architecture:

```text
Persona Interface
→ Relay
→ Steward
→ runtime session / work unit / dispatch
```

Return path:

```text
system output
→ Relay return package
→ Persona Interface response package
→ user-facing response
```

## 4.2 Why V17 matters

ION’s runtime cannot be production-relevant if it only runs hidden file transformations. It must have a lawful front door.

V17 proved that the front door could be split into semantic roles:

```text
Persona Interface = user-facing renderer
Relay = semantic-boundary translator
Steward = graph-native orchestrator
```

This prevents the common failure mode where “the assistant” becomes user persona, semantic router, execution authority, memory surface, and reviewer all at once.

## 4.3 What V17 did not prove

V17 did not prove:

```text
full product UX
production API
browser/dashboard interface
general workflow operation
source-summary rewrite authority
agent activation authority
```

## 4.4 Production implication

The Persona/Relay/Steward split should be preserved and promoted through ratification.

The demo-specific front-door path should be extracted into production primitives before product launch.

---

## 5. V26 — Complete Summary Refresh Bounded Commit Demo

**Lineage status:** complete six-phase demo path  
**Claim class:** `[DEMO-PROVEN]` and partially `[RUNTIME-PROVEN]`  
**Production status:** certified workflow seed, not generalized workflow runtime

## 5.1 What V26 proved

V26 completed the six-phase summary-refresh demo path:

```text
front-door ingress
→ template request
→ completion witness
→ reaction selection
→ projection-only index surface
→ proposal-only graph writeback surface
→ governed review verdict surface
→ bounded graph-state commit
→ persona return
```

This was the first complete bounded workflow chain behind the front door.

## 5.2 Why V26 matters

V26 proves that ION can take a user-level request and turn it into a lawful graph-state update under bounded rules.

The important phrase is:

```text
bounded graph-state commit
```

V26 commits into a bounded evented-template graph-state surface. It does not rewrite source summaries and does not claim global graph canon.

## 5.3 What V26 did not prove

V26 did not prove:

```text
global graph canon
source-summary rewrite authority
arbitrary workflow generality
daemon production safety
subagent fan-out/fan-in
production release status
```

## 5.4 Production implication

V26 is the workflow extraction source.

Production must split:

```text
summary_refresh_demo.py
```

into:

```text
evented_workflow_runner.py
summary_refresh_workflow.py
summary_refresh_demo.py
```

The demo adapter should remain. The production primitive must be generalized.

---

## 6. V27 — Replay CLI

**Lineage status:** replay infrastructure  
**Claim class:** `[RUNTIME-PROVEN]` / `[A4-DEMO]`  
**Production status:** release-demo infrastructure, candidate production pattern

## 6.1 What V27 proved

V27 added a single-command replay surface:

```bash
PYTHONPATH=ION/04_packages python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_replay --workspace-root .
```

It made the full summary-refresh demo path executable from a CLI and produced replay reports.

## 6.2 Why V27 matters

A demo that cannot be replayed is not stable evidence.

V27 turned the runtime proof into something an operator or another agent could run.

## 6.3 Important repeat-run boundary

V27 discovered a real safety boundary:

```text
A repeated LAND replay may refuse to overwrite existing bounded graph-state entries.
```

This is correct. It prevents silent overwrite.

## 6.4 What V27 did not prove

V27 did not prove:

```text
fresh workspace isolation
operator-safe repeated project-root validation
certification
evidence packaging
production release
```

## 6.5 Production implication

Replay should become a generalized workflow primitive:

```text
workflow_replay_runner.py
```

The summary-refresh replay remains a demo wrapper.

---

## 7. V28 — Replay Doctor

**Lineage status:** operator validation infrastructure  
**Claim class:** `[RUNTIME-PROVEN]` / `[A4-DEMO]`  
**Production status:** doctor pattern source

## 7.1 What V28 proved

V28 added a doctor command that validates the replay demo in two modes:

```text
project-root smoke:
  no bounded commit

isolated full commit:
  tiny fresh workspace
  copied contract projection
  full LAND bounded commit path
```

## 7.2 Why V28 matters

V28 solved the repeat-run problem discovered in V27.

The project root might already contain bounded graph-state entries. A safe operator doctor should not try to overwrite them. Instead, it should:

```text
prove project-root path without commit
prove full commit in isolated sandbox
```

## 7.3 What V28 did not prove

V28 did not prove:

```text
certification verdict
portable evidence bundle
release-candidate packaging
independent verification
production readiness
```

## 7.4 Production implication

Doctor logic should be generalized:

```text
workflow_doctor.py
```

Every production workflow should eventually have a doctor mode.

---

## 8. V29 — Certification Gate

**Lineage status:** certification infrastructure  
**Claim class:** `[RUNTIME-PROVEN]` / `[A4-DEMO]`  
**Production status:** certification primitive source

## 8.1 What V29 proved

V29 added a certification command/report.

The certification gate returns `CERTIFIED` only when:

```text
release readiness is READY
project-root no-commit smoke passes
isolated full LAND bounded commit passes
isolated commit has >=1 bounded commit
isolated commit has >=2 committed nodes
isolated commit has >=4 committed edges
forbidden mutation boundaries remain false
```

## 8.2 Why V29 matters

V29 made evidence consumable as a verdict.

This is the transition from:

```text
the demo seems to work
```

to:

```text
the demo passes a declared certification gate
```

## 8.3 Stability fix

V29 also fixed deterministic project-root smoke collisions by making the doctor’s project-root smoke explicitly non-dispatching.

This is important because production ION must handle repeated validation without corrupting runtime state.

## 8.4 What V29 did not prove

V29 did not prove:

```text
evidence portability
release-candidate packaging
independent capsule verification
full production readiness
```

## 8.5 Production implication

Certification logic should be generalized:

```text
workflow_certification_gate.py
```

Certification gates should become standard across all serious workflows.

---

## 9. V30 — Evidence Bundle

**Lineage status:** evidence packaging infrastructure  
**Claim class:** `[RUNTIME-PROVEN]` / `[A4-DEMO]`  
**Production status:** evidence primitive source

## 9.1 What V30 proved

V30 added an evidence-bundle command that packages certification, doctor, and replay reports into a self-contained bundle.

Typical bundle contents:

```text
summary_refresh_demo_evidence_bundle_manifest.json
README.md
reports/<certification-report>.json
reports/<doctor-report>.json
reports/<project-root-smoke-replay-report>.json
reports/<isolated-full-commit-replay-report>.json
```

## 9.2 Why V30 matters

Certification without portable evidence is fragile.

V30 lets the proof travel.

## 9.3 What V30 did not prove

V30 did not prove:

```text
release-candidate capsule integrity
checksum verification
independent verification
production readiness
```

## 9.4 Production implication

Evidence bundling should be generalized:

```text
evidence_bundle_builder.py
```

Evidence bundles should be standard for production gates.

```text
evidence_bundle/
```

## 10.2 Why V31 matters

V31 turned evidence into a release-review object.

It created a handoff package that can be inspected, checksummed, and run by an operator or reviewer.

## 10.3 What V31 did not prove

```text
release candidate directory exists

COMMANDS.sh exists
CHECKSUMS.sha256 exists
copied evidence_bundle/ directory exists
checksums match all files listed in CHECKSUMS.sha256
required commands are present
forbidden boundary claims remain false
```

## 11.2 Why V32 matters

V32 is the first point at which the release-demo path becomes independently verifiable after packaging.

That makes V32 the correct certified demo baseline.

## 11.3 What V32 does not prove

```text
agent activation authority
```

```text
certified demo baseline
```

not:

```text

```

This distinction must appear near the top of the encyclopedia.
