# Volume II — Production Readiness

## 1. Why This Part Exists

This production encyclopedia must be able to say two things at the same time:

```text
ION has crossed from doctrine into certified runtime evidence.
ION is not yet production-ready.
```

Those statements are not contradictory. They are the only honest posture.

A system may have a verified release-demo capsule and still lack production authority. ION now has a certified, replayable, doctorable, evidence-bundled, release-candidate-packaged, independently verifiable demo spine. That is a major threshold. It proves that the living context graph doctrine can be enacted as a bounded workflow.

But production readiness requires more than one certified workflow. It requires that the system’s authority model, graph model, mutation rights, agent activation, daemon safety, release packaging, and adversarial review all be generalized, ratified, and tested.

The purpose of this part is to prevent the certified demo from being laundered into a production claim.

---

## 2. Production Readiness Definition

ION is production-ready only when it can safely run real user/project work through governed graph operations without hidden authority drift, unreviewed mutation, unsafe agent activation, unrecoverable daemon behavior, stale role relapse, or unverifiable release state.

More formally:

```text
ION is production-ready when all production authority surfaces are ratified,
all mutation paths are governed and reversible,
all graph writes occur under canonical graph law,
all agent/subagent activation is leased, bounded, auditable, and kill-switchable,
the daemon can run, pause, resume, recover, and prove its actions,
the product front door exposes user-visible explanation and review surfaces,
and adversarial audit finds no critical blockers.
```

Production readiness is therefore not a mood, milestone label, or demo verdict. It is a multi-gate state.

---

## 3. Current Verdict

```text
NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
```

This is the correct verdict after V33.

The production-readiness verdict remains negative because the following are still incomplete:

```text
A3 surface ratification
demo/production primitive split
global graph canon
source-summary rewrite authority
agent/subagent activation authority
production daemon loop
adversarial production audit
```

The fact that these gaps are now named is progress. V33 creates a gate. It does not pass the gate.

---

## 4. Why V32 Is a Certified Demo Baseline, Not Production Completion

V32 verifies an existing release-candidate capsule. It checks structure, manifest validity, command presence, copied evidence, checksum consistency, and forbidden boundary claims.

That means V32 can say:

```text
This demo release candidate is structurally intact, checksum-consistent, certified, and evidence-backed.
```

V32 cannot say:

```text
ION is production-ready.
```

## 4.1 What V32 certifies

V32 certifies the release-demo path:

```text
front-door
→ template
→ event
→ reaction
→ projection
→ proposal
→ review
→ bounded commit
→ replay
→ doctor
→ certification
→ evidence bundle
→ release candidate
→ verifier
```

This is the correct certified demo baseline.

## 4.2 What V32 does not certify

V32 does not certify:

```text
global graph canon
source-summary rewrite authority
general workflow runtime
agent/subagent activation authority
production daemon safety
full product UI/API
constitutional ratification of A3 surfaces
```

## 4.3 The production encyclopedia rule

The production encyclopedia must use this language:

```text
V32 is the certified demo baseline.
```

It must not use this language:

```text
V32 is the production baseline.
```

---

## 5. Why V33 Is the Current Production-Readiness Frame

V33 adds the production-readiness charter and ratification matrix. Its core value is that it prevents the system from calling itself production-ready too early.

V33 establishes:

```text
baseline lock
production-readiness charter
ratification matrix protocol
production-readiness gap register
production-readiness report generator
production-readiness readiness checks
```

It also names:

```text
production verdict = NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
next move = V34_A3_SURFACE_RATIFICATION_PASS
```

## 5.1 What V33 proves

V33 proves that ION now has a production-readiness gate.

## 5.2 What V33 does not prove

V33 does not prove that the gate has been passed.

## 5.3 Why this matters

Without V33, the certified demo could create pressure to overclaim. With V33, ION preserves the distinction between:

```text
certified release demo
production system
```

That distinction is itself a sign of system maturity.

---

## 6. Production Readiness Gate Families

Production readiness requires at least seven gate families.

## 6.1 Gate Family 1 — Authority Ratification

Production ION cannot be governed by accidental authority.

Every production-relevant surface must be classified:

```text
A1 crown law
A2 production governance
A3 operational proposal
A4 demo/evidence infrastructure
historical-only
deprecated
blocked
```

Required evidence:

```text
ratification matrix
source paths
authority class
mutation rights
runtime rights
reviewer verdict
contradiction status
```

Production rule:

```text
No provisional A3 surface may control production mutation without ratification.
```

## 6.2 Gate Family 2 — Demo/Production Primitive Split

The summary-refresh demo proves a path. Production needs reusable primitives.

Required split:

```text
demo adapter
workflow primitive
product workflow
evidence/release infrastructure
```

Production rule:

```text
Demo-proven code may inform production primitives but must not be promoted blindly.
```

## 6.3 Gate Family 3 — Global Graph Canon

ION’s root substrate is a living context graph, but production requires explicit graph canon.

Required graph layers:

```text
source graph
working graph
proposal graph
review graph
bounded commit graph
canonical context graph
release/evidence graph
agent memory/context graph
```

Production rule:

```text
No global graph write occurs until graph canon is ratified.
```

## 6.4 Gate Family 4 — Source Summary Rewrite Authority

ION must eventually update its own summaries, but canonical source-summary rewrite is dangerous.

Required path:

```text
source material
→ draft summary
→ diff
→ provenance map
→ contradiction scan
→ review verdict
→ bounded patch proposal
→ source-summary commit
→ rollback receipt
→ index/graph update
```

Production rule:

```text
No model may rewrite canonical source summaries directly.
```

## 6.5 Gate Family 5 — Agent/Subagent Activation Authority

ION cannot scale if a few agents must hold everything. It needs graph-region custody, domain managers, specialists, and contextual node workers.

But production activation requires:

```text
activation authority
context package
region permission
mutation rights
lease duration
heartbeat
budget
result receipt
kill switch
conflict escalation
fan-in review
```

Production rule:

```text
No autonomous agent/subagent activation occurs without lease, context, receipt, and kill-switch law.
```

## 6.6 Gate Family 6 — Production Daemon Loop

A production daemon must not merely run scripts. It must run lawfully.

Required properties:

```text
idempotency
queue locking
duplicate detection
crash recovery
resume from receipts
safe mode
operator pause/resume
health check
audit log
dry-run mode
```

Production rule:

```text
A task can be started, interrupted, resumed, and verified without corrupting graph state.
```

## 6.7 Gate Family 7 — Adversarial Production Audit

Production readiness cannot be self-declared. It must survive adversarial review.

Audit targets:

```text
stale authority
Codex role relapse
alias drift
unratified A3 mutation path
duplicate graph writes
checksum tampering
missing receipts
unsafe source rewrite
unsafe agent activation
daemon replay collision
front-door role mixing
broken manifest references
contradictory summaries
```

Production rule:

```text
Production cannot be claimed while any critical adversarial finding remains open.
```

---

|---|---|---|---|---|
| G1 | A3 surface ratification | incomplete | provisional surfaces may be overpromoted | V34 |
| G2 | Demo/production primitive split | incomplete | demo code may be mistaken for production primitive | V35 |
| G3 | Global graph canon | not ratified | bounded graph state may be confused with canon | V36 |
| G4 | Source-summary rewrite authority | not implemented | source mutation unsafe | V37–V38 |
| G5 | Agent/subagent activation authority | not implemented | distributed context operations unsafe | V39–V40 |
| G6 | Production daemon loop | incomplete | runtime recovery/idempotency not fully hardened | V41 |
| G7 | Adversarial production audit | incomplete | production claim untested against hostile review | V43 |

## 11. Production Readiness Anti-Claims

The production encyclopedia should explicitly forbid these statements until future evidence exists.

```text
ION is production-ready.
ION has global graph canon.
ION can safely rewrite source summaries.
ION can activate arbitrary subagents.
ION has a production daemon.
ION has passed adversarial production audit.
All A3 surfaces are ratified.
The summary-refresh demo is the production runtime.
The release-demo verifier is constitutional ratification.
```

Correct alternatives:

```text
ION has a certified demo baseline.
ION has a production-readiness gate.
ION has named production gaps.
ION has a lawful path toward production readiness.
```

## 12. Production Readiness Chapter Insert for Full Encyclopedia

The following chapter should be inserted into the full production encyclopedia.

## Chapter: Why ION Is Not Yet Production-Ready

ION is not yet production-ready because production readiness is not the same as architectural coherence, conceptual maturity, or a certified demo.

The certified demo proves that ION can enact a bounded graph workflow through the full chain of front-door intake, template instantiation, event completion, reaction selection, projection, proposal, review, bounded commit, replay, doctor validation, certification, evidence bundling, release-candidate packaging, and independent verification.

That is significant. It means ION’s root doctrine has crossed into enacted runtime.

But production readiness requires generalized and ratified authority. It must be clear which surfaces can mutate graph state, which can only propose, which are demo-only, which are historical, and which are production primitives. ION must also define global graph canon, safe source-summary rewrite authority, agent and subagent activation law, production daemon safety, product operator visibility, and adversarial audit gates.

Calling ION production-ready before those gates pass would violate ION’s own doctrine.

Therefore the correct current verdict is:

```text
NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
```

This verdict is not a downgrade. It is evidence that ION can now hold itself to production law.

```text
ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_RATIFICATION_MATRIX_DRAFT.md
```

---

# Volume III — Ratification Matrix

## 1. Why the Ratification Matrix Exists

ION is now complex enough that prose alone cannot safely govern it.

The current production encyclopedia can explain that ION is a living context graph, that files can become evented graph objects, that a front-door request can travel through Persona Interface, Relay, and Steward, and that the summary-refresh demo can be replayed, doctored, certified, bundled, packaged, and verified. But explanation is not ratification.

A production system needs a matrix because every major object must answer:

```text
What is this?
Where did it come from?
Is it doctrine, runtime, demo, evidence, historical residue, or production law?
Can it mutate anything?
Can it route runtime work?
Can it activate agents?
Can it write graph state?
Can it rewrite source summaries?
Can it be used in production?
What evidence supports it?
What review is still required?
```

The ratification matrix prevents three common failure modes:

```text
1. demo proof laundering into production authority
2. historical names reentering live authority
3. provisional concepts being treated as ratified law because they are useful
```

The matrix is therefore a production safety organ.

---

## 2. Ratification Classes

| Class | Meaning | Production use |
|---|---|---|
| `A1` | crown/constitutional authority | highest law, cannot be rewritten by operational runtime |
| `A2` | ratified production governance / production primitive | may govern production behavior within its scope |
| `A3` | operational proposal / current-phase working surface | may be used for bounded development and proposal work, not unreviewed production mutation |
| `A4` | demo, evidence, release-demo, or verifier infrastructure | may prove or package demo behavior, not automatically production law |
| `P` | provisional semantic object | conceptually important, requires ratification |
| `G` | production-gated required capability | required before production, not yet complete |
| `H` | historical-only lineage | preserved for archaeology, not current live authority |
| `D` | deprecated / removed | must not be used except for migration or audit |
| `B` | blocked pending contradiction/audit | cannot be promoted until resolved |

---

## 3. Rights Columns

Every row should eventually specify rights.

| Right | Meaning |
|---|---|
| `read_rights` | may be read as context |
| `explain_rights` | may be used in explanatory documentation |
| `proposal_rights` | may generate proposals |
| `review_rights` | may participate in review |
| `bounded_commit_rights` | may commit inside bounded/non-canonical surfaces |
| `canonical_write_rights` | may mutate canonical production state |
| `source_rewrite_rights` | may rewrite canonical summaries/source-doc surfaces |
| `agent_activation_rights` | may activate or spawn agents/subagents |
| `release_rights` | may package, certify, or verify release candidates |

Default production rule:

```text
No object receives canonical_write_rights, source_rewrite_rights, or agent_activation_rights unless explicitly ratified.
```

---

## 4. Matrix: Root Concepts and Doctrinal Objects

| Object | Current class | Proposed production class | Rights | Evidence | Required review | Current verdict |
|---|---:|---:|---|---|---|---|
| Living Context Graph Substrate | `P` | `A2` candidate | read, explain, proposal | restored root invariant, encyclopedia lineage, runtime alignment | semantic/constitutional review | keep provisional pending ratification |
| Lawful AI Operating Substrate | `P` | `A2` candidate | read, explain, proposal | current doctrine and architecture | constitutional review | keep provisional |
| Evented Template File Graph | `A3` / runtime-proven | `A2` candidate | read, explain, proposal, bounded commit | V10/V26 lineage | runtime + graph canon review | promote after primitive split |
| Template-Instantiated Graph Object | `A3` | `A2` candidate | read, explain, proposal | V10/V26 event flow | template contract review | keep and formalize |
| Completion Event | `A3` runtime primitive | `A2` candidate | bounded event generation | completion-event tests | kernel review | candidate for promotion |
| Reaction Selection | `A3` runtime primitive | `A2` candidate | bounded reaction proposal | reaction-selection tests | kernel review | candidate for promotion |
| Projection Surface | `A3` runtime primitive | `A2` candidate | projection-only | index projection tests | graph canon review | keep bounded |

```yaml
    - HISTORICAL_ONLY

    - DEPRECATE

  rationale:
```

---

# Volume III — Demo-to-Production Primitive Split

## 1. Why This Split Is Required

The V26–V32 runtime line proves something very important:

```text
ION can run a bounded, certified, verifiable graph workflow from user front door through template, event, reaction, projection, proposal, review, bounded commit, evidence bundle, release candidate, and independent verification.
```

But this proof is still organized around a particular demo/product path:

```text
summary refresh
```

That path is not arbitrary. Summary refresh is a good first workflow because ION’s core value depends on self-documentation, context maintenance, graph-aware summaries, and lawful updating of project knowledge. But production ION cannot be a bundle of hard-coded summary-refresh demo modules.

The split is required because:

```text
demo-specific proof must be preserved
production-general primitives must be extracted
product workflows must remain explicit
release/evidence infrastructure must be generalized
authority must not be overpromoted
```

The core risk is demo laundering:

```text
A demo proves a bounded case.
The bounded case gets called a production primitive.
The production primitive receives broad mutation rights.
The system bypasses ratification.
```

The split prevents that.

---

## 2. Four-Layer Separation Model

Every current V26–V32 demo/release surface should be classified into four layers.

## 2.1 Demo Adapter

A demo adapter is a narrow implementation that proves a particular path.

Example:

```text
summary_refresh_demo.py
```

It may be retained forever as a certified demo surface.

It should not automatically become the production workflow runtime.

## 2.2 Production Primitive

A production primitive is reusable infrastructure extracted from the demo path.

Example target:

```text
evented_workflow_runner.py
```

A production primitive must be:

```text
workflow-neutral
contract-bound
testable outside summary refresh
authority-classified
reviewed
ratified before production mutation
```

## 2.3 Product Workflow

A product workflow is a real task family built from production primitives.

Example target:

```text
summary_refresh_workflow.py
```

It may remain summary-specific, but should depend on generalized primitives rather than demo-only code.

## 2.4 Release / Evidence Infrastructure

Release/evidence infrastructure packages and verifies proof.

Example targets:

```text
evidence_bundle_builder.py
release_candidate_builder.py
release_candidate_verifier.py
```

These should become reusable across workflows.

---

## 3. Extraction Law

The production encyclopedia should preserve the following law:

```text
Extraction is not promotion.
```

This means:

```text
A primitive extracted from demo code does not become A2 production governance merely by being generalized.
```

It must pass:

```text
tests
review
ratification
authority classification
mutation-rights assignment
adversarial audit where needed
```

Therefore the correct chain is:

```text
demo surface
→ extraction proposal
→ generic primitive draft
→ workflow-specific adapter retained
→ tests across at least two workflows
→ ratification review
→ authority-class promotion if accepted
```

Not:

```text
demo surface
→ rename
→ production primitive
```

---

## 4. Summary of Current Demo Spine

The current certified demo spine is:

```text
front-door ingress
→ summary-refresh request template
→ template completion event
→ reaction selection
→ projection-only index surface
→ proposal-only graph writeback surface
→ governed review verdict
→ bounded graph-state commit
→ persona return
→ replay CLI
→ replay doctor
→ certification gate
→ evidence bundle
→ release-candidate capsule
→ release-candidate verifier
→ production-readiness charter
```

The spine proves the architecture, but it contains multiple different kinds of surfaces:

```text
front-door surfaces
workflow surfaces
template/event surfaces
graph proposal/review/commit surfaces
operator replay/doctor surfaces
certification/evidence/release surfaces
readiness/ratification surfaces
```

Production readiness requires each family to be extracted and classified separately.

---

## 5. Current-to-Target Extraction Table

| Current surface | Current role | Target primitive | Target product/demo wrapper | Production status |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `summary_refresh_demo.py` | demo workflow runner | `evented_workflow_runner.py` | `summary_refresh_workflow.py`, `summary_refresh_demo.py` | extract in V35 |
| `summary_refresh_demo_replay.py` | replay CLI for demo | `workflow_replay_runner.py` | `summary_refresh_replay.py` | extract in V35 |
| `summary_refresh_demo_doctor.py` | two-mode demo doctor | `workflow_doctor.py` | `summary_refresh_doctor.py` | extract in V35 |
| `summary_refresh_demo_certification.py` | demo certification gate | `workflow_certification_gate.py` | `summary_refresh_certification.py` | extract in V35 |
| `summary_refresh_demo_evidence_bundle.py` | demo evidence bundle | `evidence_bundle_builder.py` | `summary_refresh_evidence_bundle.py` | extract in V35 |
| `summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate.py` | demo release candidate | `release_candidate_builder.py` | `summary_refresh_release_candidate.py` | extract in V35 |
| `summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate_verify.py` | demo verifier | `release_candidate_verifier.py` | `summary_refresh_release_candidate_verify.py` | extract in V35 |
| `production_readiness.py` | readiness report/gate | `production_readiness_gate.py` | `ion_production_readiness.py` | review after V34 |

---

## 6. Primitive 1 — Evented Workflow Runner

## 6.1 Current source

```text
summary_refresh_demo.py
```

## 6.2 Target primitive

```text
evented_workflow_runner.py
```

## 6.3 Purpose

The evented workflow runner should provide a general runtime skeleton:

```text
front-door input or internal request
→ template instantiation
→ contract validation
→ completion event
→ reaction selection
→ projection
→ proposal
→ review
→ bounded commit if authorized
→ return package
→ receipt
```

## 6.4 Required generic inputs

```yaml
workflow_definition:
  workflow_id:
  template_id:
  contract_id:
  input_schema:
  output_schema:
  allowed_reactions:
  projection_policy:
  proposal_policy:
  review_policy:
  commit_policy:
  return_policy:
  receipt_policy:
```

## 6.5 Required outputs

```yaml
workflow_run_result:
  workflow_run_id:
  workflow_id:
  request_path:
  completion_events:
  selected_reactions:
  projections:
  proposals:
  reviews:
  commits:
  receipts:
  return_package:
  boundary_claims:
```

## 6.6 Production constraints

The primitive may not assume:

```text
summary refresh
one template only
one graph region only
LAND as default
source rewrite permission
canonical graph permission
agent activation permission
```

## 6.7 Tests required before promotion

```text
can run summary-refresh workflow
can run at least one non-summary workflow
HOLD prevents commit
ESCALATE prevents commit
invalid template blocks event
missing contract blocks run
forbidden reaction is refused
bounded commit cannot overwrite existing state silently
canonical write is refused unless explicitly authorized
```

---

## 7. Primitive 2 — Workflow Replay Runner

## 7.1 Current source

```text
summary_refresh_demo_replay.py
```

## 7.2 Target primitive

```text
workflow_replay_runner.py
```

## 7.3 Purpose

The replay runner should rerun a workflow path from a defined state and produce a replay report.

Generic command pattern:

```bash
python -S -m kernel.workflow_replay --workspace-root . --workflow-id <workflow>
```

## 7.4 Required properties

```text
deterministic where requested
safe project-root no-dispatch mode
fresh workspace mode
non-overwrite policy
full JSON report
human-readable summary
explicit boundary claims
```

## 7.5 What it must not do

```text
silently mutate canonical graph state
redispatch already-dispatched front-door queue entries
overwrite bounded graph-state files
claim certification
claim production readiness
```

---

## 8. Primitive 3 — Workflow Doctor

## 8.1 Current source

```text
summary_refresh_demo_doctor.py
```

## 8.2 Target primitive

```text
workflow_doctor.py
```

## 8.3 Purpose

The doctor validates a workflow in safe modes.

Generic two-mode pattern:

```text
project-root smoke:
  no commit, no dispatch, evidence only

isolated full path:
  fresh sandbox, full bounded path, proof of commit where expected
```

## 8.4 Required properties

```text
can diagnose readiness
can run no-commit project smoke
can run isolated full commit
can prove the isolated commit did not touch project-root graph state
can produce report
can support blocked/failed mode
```

## 8.5 Production implication

Every production workflow should eventually have a doctor.

---

## 9. Primitive 4 — Workflow Certification Gate

## 9.1 Current source

```text
summary_refresh_demo_certification.py
```

## 9.2 Target primitive

```text
workflow_certification_gate.py
```

## 9.3 Purpose

The certification gate turns doctor/replay evidence into a verdict.

Generic verdicts:

```text
CERTIFIED
BLOCKED
```

## 9.4 Required evidence model

```yaml
certification_requirements:
  readiness_allowed:
  project_smoke_passed:
  isolated_full_run_passed:
  required_commits:
  required_nodes:
  required_edges:
  forbidden_boundary_claims:
  workflow_specific_assertions:
```

## 9.5 Production constraints

Certification does not equal ratification.

A certified workflow proves its declared evidence requirements. It does not automatically gain production mutation rights.

---

## 10. Primitive 5 — Evidence Bundle Builder

## 10.1 Current source

```text
summary_refresh_demo_evidence_bundle.py
```

## 10.2 Target primitive

```text
evidence_bundle_builder.py
```

## 10.3 Purpose

The evidence bundle builder packages:

```text
certification report
doctor report
replay reports
readiness summary
commands
boundary claims
manifest
README
```

## 10.4 Required properties

```text
copy-only behavior
missing report safety
blocked evidence support when explicitly allowed
machine-readable manifest
human-readable README
checksums where appropriate
```

## 10.5 Production constraints

Evidence bundles do not mutate runtime state. They package proof.

---

## 11. Primitive 6 — Release Candidate Builder

## 11.1 Current source

```text
summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate.py
```

## 11.2 Target primitive

```text
release_candidate_builder.py
```

## 11.3 Purpose

The release candidate builder packages evidence into a reviewable capsule.

Generic capsule contents:

```text
release_candidate_manifest.json
README.md
COMMANDS.sh
CHECKSUMS.sha256
evidence_bundle/
```

## 11.4 Required properties

```text
certified evidence required unless blocked mode explicit
checksums over all capsule files
command reference
boundary statement
copy of evidence bundle
stable manifest schema
```

## 11.5 Production constraints

A release candidate is not production unless the production release gate says so.

---

## 12. Primitive 7 — Release Candidate Verifier

## 12.1 Current source

```text
summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate_verify.py
```

## 12.2 Target primitive

```text
release_candidate_verifier.py
```

## 12.3 Purpose

The verifier independently checks an existing release-candidate capsule.

Required checks:

```text
capsule directory exists
manifest exists/readable
verdict/certified status valid
README exists
COMMANDS exists
CHECKSUMS exists
evidence bundle exists
checksums match
required commands present
boundary claims valid
```

## 12.4 Production constraints

Verification does not rerun the workflow. It checks the package.

A verified demo release candidate is still demo evidence unless the release candidate is explicitly a production release candidate.

---

## 13. Primitive 8 — Production Readiness Gate

## 13.1 Current source

```text
production_readiness.py
```

## 13.2 Target primitive

```text
production_readiness_gate.py
```

## 13.3 Purpose

The production readiness gate reports whether ION has passed production requirements.

Current verdict:

```text
NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
```

## 13.4 Required future checks

```text
all A3 surfaces classified
demo primitives split
graph canon ratified
source rewrite authority implemented
agent activation law implemented
daemon safety proven
adversarial audit passed
production release candidate verified
```

## 13.5 Production constraints

This gate must remain capable of saying no.

If it cannot say no, it is not a gate.

---

## 14. Product Workflow Layer

After primitive extraction, summary refresh should remain as a product workflow.

Target:

```text
summary_refresh_workflow.py
```

Purpose:

```text
maintain project summaries through lawful proposal, review, and bounded mutation.
```

But production summary refresh has two stages.

## 14.1 Stage A — Current demo/product stage

```text
summary request
→ evented template path
→ bounded graph-state commit
```

This is V26/V32-certified as demo path.

## 14.2 Stage B — Future production source-summary rewrite

```text
source material
→ draft summary
→ diff
→ provenance
→ contradiction scan
→ review
→ source-summary patch commit
→ rollback receipt
```

Stage B is blocked until V37–V38.

Production rule:

```text
Summary refresh may update bounded graph-state demo surfaces now.
It may not rewrite canonical source summaries until source-summary rewrite authority exists.
```

---

## 15. Second Workflow Requirement

A primitive cannot be considered generalized until at least one additional workflow runs through it.

Recommended second workflow:

```text
doctrine_evolution_proposal
```

Why this workflow:

```text
It is close to ION’s real development work.
It requires proposal and review.
It should not require source-summary rewrite at first.
It can produce bounded graph-state evidence.
It creates pressure for ratification and contradiction handling.
```

Candidate path:

```text
doctrine evolution request
→ doctrine proposal template
→ completion event
→ reaction selection
→ projection
→ proposal
→ review
→ bounded graph-state commit
→ evidence bundle
→ release candidate
→ verifier
```

The second workflow proves that primitives are not summary-refresh-only.

---

## 16. Third Workflow Requirement

A third workflow should test stale-surface audit.

Recommended third workflow:

```text
stale_surface_audit
```

Why this workflow:

```text
It detects obsolete authority.
It catches Codex role relapse.
It supports production ratification.
It exercises registry/protocol scanning without source rewrite.
```

Candidate path:

```text
audit request
→ stale surface audit template
→ completion event
→ reaction selection
→ projection
→ stale surface proposal
→ review
→ bounded evidence commit
```

This workflow prepares V34/V43.

---

## 17. General Workflow Definition Schema

Future workflows should be declared in a workflow registry.

```yaml
workflow_definition:
  workflow_id:
  canonical_name:
  authority_class:
  workflow_status:
    - DEMO
    - PRODUCT_CANDIDATE
    - PRODUCTION_CANDIDATE
    - RATIFIED_PRODUCTION
  template_ids: []
  allowed_inputs: []
  allowed_reactions: []
  graph_regions:
    read: []
    propose: []
    review: []
    bounded_commit: []
    canonical_write: []
  review_policy:
    required: true
    allowed_verdicts:
      - LAND
      - HOLD
      - ESCALATE
  commit_policy:
    bounded_only: true
    canonical_write: false
    source_rewrite: false
    overwrite_policy: refuse
  evidence_policy:
    replay_required: true
    doctor_required: true
    certification_required: true
    release_candidate_required: false
    verifier_required: false
```

---

## 18. Proposed V35 Outputs

V35 should produce:

```text
ION/02_architecture/DEMO_TO_PRODUCTION_PRIMITIVE_SPLIT_PROTOCOL.md
ION/03_registry/workflow_definition_registry.yaml
ION/04_packages/kernel/evented_workflow_runner.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/workflow_replay_runner.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/workflow_doctor.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/workflow_certification_gate.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/evidence_bundle_builder.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/release_candidate_builder.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/release_candidate_verifier.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/production_readiness_gate.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_evented_workflow_runner.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_workflow_replay_runner.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_workflow_doctor.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_workflow_certification_gate.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_release_infrastructure_generic.py
```

Demo wrappers should remain:

```text
summary_refresh_demo.py
summary_refresh_demo_replay.py
summary_refresh_demo_doctor.py
summary_refresh_demo_certification.py
summary_refresh_demo_evidence_bundle.py
summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate.py
summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate_verify.py
```

But they should call generic primitives.

---

## 19. Migration Strategy

## 19.1 Do not rewrite everything at once

The correct migration path is:

```text
copy behavior into generic primitive
make demo wrapper call primitive
run old tests unchanged
add generic primitive tests
add second workflow tests
only then classify primitive for ratification
```

## 19.2 Maintain backward-compatible demo commands

Existing commands should continue to work:

```bash
python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_replay --workspace-root .
python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_doctor --workspace-root .
python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_certification --workspace-root .
python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_evidence_bundle --workspace-root .
python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate --workspace-root .
python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate_verify --workspace-root .
```

They may internally delegate to generic primitives after V35.

## 19.3 Add generic commands

New generic commands may be:

```bash
python -S -m kernel.workflow_replay --workspace-root . --workflow-id summary_refresh
python -S -m kernel.workflow_doctor --workspace-root . --workflow-id summary_refresh
python -S -m kernel.workflow_certify --workspace-root . --workflow-id summary_refresh
```

## 19.4 Preserve evidence identity

The release-demo evidence lineage should remain traceable. A generic primitive must not obscure the fact that V26–V32 proved the summary-refresh path.

---

## 20. Anti-Patterns

## 20.1 Rename-only promotion

Bad:

```text
summary_refresh_demo.py -> evented_workflow_runner.py
```

without changing assumptions.

## 20.2 Hidden broadening

Bad:

```text
a function that used to write bounded demo state quietly gains canonical write permission
```

## 20.3 Source rewrite smuggling

Bad:

```text
summary refresh starts editing canonical source summaries because the name implies refresh
```

## 20.4 Agent activation smuggling

Bad:

```text
workflow doctor starts spawning subagents without activation law
```

## 20.5 Certification inflation

Bad:

```text
CERTIFIED means production-ready
```

Correct:

```text
CERTIFIED means declared evidence requirements passed.
```

---

## 21. Acceptance Criteria for the Split

The demo-to-production primitive split is successful when:

```text
1. Existing summary-refresh demo commands still pass.
2. Generic primitives exist and are independently tested.
3. Summary-refresh wrappers call generic primitives.
4. At least one second workflow runs through the generic evented workflow runner.
5. Demo surfaces remain A4 until ratified.
6. Generic primitives remain A3/A2-candidate until ratified.
7. No canonical graph write is introduced.
8. No source-summary rewrite is introduced.
9. No agent activation is introduced.
10. Release/evidence infrastructure remains checksum/verifier compatible.
```

---

## 22. Production Encyclopedia Insertion Guidance

This part should appear after the ratification matrix and before the graph canon part.

Reason:

```text
The reader must first know what surfaces are classified as demo/provisional/production-gated.
Then the reader can understand how demo surfaces become production primitives.
Only then should the encyclopedia explain graph canon, source rewrite, and agent activation.
```

---

## 23. Chapter Insert for Full Encyclopedia

## Chapter: Demo Proof Is Not Production Authority

ION’s certified summary-refresh demo is a real proof. It shows that a user-facing request can become a template-instantiated graph object, create an event, select reactions, project index state, propose graph writes, receive review, commit bounded graph state, return to the user, and be replayed, doctored, certified, bundled, packaged, and verified.

That is enough to prove the architecture can operate.

It is not enough to prove that every part of the demo path is a production primitive.

The demo path contains narrow assumptions: a specific workflow, a specific template family, a specific graph region, a specific bounded commit target, a specific evidence model, and a specific release-demo status. Production ION must extract the reusable machinery from that path while preserving the demo as evidence.

The split matters because ION is designed to prevent authority drift. If a demo module can become production law merely by being useful, then ION has failed its own doctrine. Therefore extraction must proceed through proposal, generic primitive tests, additional workflow proof, ratification review, and explicit rights assignment.

The right conclusion is:

```text
The summary-refresh demo is certified evidence.
The production primitive must be extracted and ratified.
```

---

## 24. Next Artifact

The next encyclopedia artifact should be:

```text
ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_GRAPH_CANON_DRAFT.md
```

Purpose:

```text
define graph canon, graph layers, write authority, graph.py adapter status, canonical graph boundaries, rollback, migration, conflict handling, and why bounded evented graph-state commit is not global graph canon.
```


---

# Volume IV — Graph Canon

## 1. Why Graph Canon Is a Production Gate

ION’s recovered root invariant is:

```text
ION is a living context graph operated by lawful agents through templates.
```

This is the correct conceptual center, but production cannot operate on a metaphor. Production requires graph canon.

Graph canon answers:

```text
What is the graph?
What are its layers?
Which files or records are nodes?
Which relationships are edges?
Which graph states are temporary?
Which graph states are proposals?
Which graph states are review-only?
Which graph states are bounded commits?
Which graph states are canonical?
Who can write each layer?
What does rollback mean?
What happens when two graph facts contradict?
What happens when a historical alias conflicts with a current truename?
```

Without graph canon, ION risks confusing these distinct things:

```text
the living context graph substrate
the kernel graph.py module
the evented template file graph
the bounded graph-state commit surface
the index projection
the release/evidence graph
the future canonical context graph
```

Production graph canon exists to prevent those surfaces from collapsing.

---

## 2. Core Graph Distinctions

The production encyclopedia must preserve these distinctions.

## 2.1 Living Context Graph

The living context graph is the system-level substrate.

It includes:

```text
files
templates
packets
receipts
registries
agents
roles
summaries
questions
events
reviews
commits
release artifacts
context packages
semantic identities
authority classes
```

It is broader than any one runtime module.

Current status:

```text
[PROVISIONAL] restored root invariant
[PRODUCTION-GATED] requires ratification before canonical production authority
```

## 2.2 Kernel graph.py

`graph.py` is an enacted runtime surface or adapter. It may implement graph operations, but it is not automatically the entire living context graph.

Current status:

```text
runtime module / adapter candidate
requires comparison report before production canon
```

Production rule:

```text
Do not equate graph.py with the whole living context graph.
```

## 2.3 Evented Template File Graph

The evented template file graph is the runtime-proven path where completed template files can create completion events, reaction selections, projections, proposals, reviews, and bounded graph-state commits.

Current status:

```text
[RUNTIME-PROVEN] bounded path
[DEMO-PROVEN] summary-refresh release-demo path
[PRODUCTION-GATED] not global canon
```

## 2.4 Bounded Graph-State Commit Surface

The bounded graph-state commit surface is the write target proven by the summary-refresh demo.

It proves:

```text
bounded write possible
reviewed commit possible
receipt-backed graph-state update possible
```

It does not prove:

```text
global graph canon
canonical source-summary rewrite
canonical production context graph mutation
```

## 2.5 Index Projection

An index projection is a derived view. It may help retrieval, audit, or validation, but it is not canon.

Production rule:

```text
Index projection is not graph canon.
```

## 2.6 Release/Evidence Graph

The release/evidence graph tracks certification reports, evidence bundles, release candidates, checksums, verification reports, and handoff packages.

It is proof infrastructure, not necessarily the canonical project graph.

---

## 3. Required Graph Layers

Production ION should define at least eight graph layers.

```text
source graph
working graph
proposal graph
review graph
bounded commit graph
canonical context graph
release/evidence graph
agent memory/context graph
```

Each layer has different rights and guarantees.

---

## 4. Source Graph

## 4.1 Definition

The source graph represents source materials and their relationships.

Source materials may include:

```text
canonical docs
runtime modules
registries
templates
receipts
historical donor artifacts
uploaded files
external returns
summaries
```

## 4.2 Current status

```text
[PRODUCTION-GATED]
```

## 4.3 Rights

Until ratified:

```text
read: allowed
explain: allowed
proposal: allowed
canonical write: blocked
source rewrite: blocked
```

## 4.4 Production rule

```text
A source graph node cannot be rewritten by a model directly.
```

Any rewrite requires source-summary rewrite authority, provenance, review, and rollback.

---

## 5. Working Graph

## 5.1 Definition

The working graph is a temporary operational graph used during active work.

It may contain:

```text
draft interpretations
candidate relationships
temporary task state
current run context
local graph projections
agent-specific working notes
```

## 5.2 Current status

```text
[PRODUCTION-GATED]
```

## 5.3 Production rule

```text
Working graph state is disposable unless promoted through proposal and review.
```

The working graph must not silently become canon.

---

## 6. Proposal Graph

## 6.1 Definition

The proposal graph contains proposed nodes, edges, changes, summaries, or authority classifications that are not yet accepted.

It is where ION can safely think in graph form without mutating canon.

## 6.2 Rights

```text
proposal writes: allowed after workflow authorization
review required: yes
canonical writes: no
source rewrites: no
```

## 6.3 Production rule

```text
Proposal graph writes are not truth claims.
```

They are candidate claims awaiting review.

---

## 7. Review Graph

## 7.1 Definition

The review graph contains judgments over proposals.

Review states may include:

```text
LAND
HOLD
ESCALATE
REJECT
NEEDS_SOURCE
NEEDS_CONTRADICTION_SCAN
NEEDS_HUMAN_REVIEW
```

## 7.2 Required structure

A review node should reference:

```text
proposal node
reviewer
authority class
verdict
rationale
required follow-up
receipt
timestamp
```

## 7.3 Production rule

```text
No proposal may become canonical solely because it exists.
```

Review mediates promotion.

---

## 8. Bounded Commit Graph

## 8.1 Definition

The bounded commit graph is a controlled commit surface where reviewed changes may land without claiming global canonical authority.

V26 proved this kind of surface.

## 8.2 Rights

```text
bounded commit: allowed when workflow and review permit
canonical write: no, unless explicitly ratified
source rewrite: no
```

## 8.3 Production rule

```text
Bounded commit is a proof and settlement surface, not automatically global canon.
```

## 8.4 Why bounded commit matters

Bounded commit lets ION act without overclaiming. It is the middle ground between:

```text
mere proposal
```

and:

```text
canonical global mutation
```

This is central to ION’s safety model.

---

## 9. Canonical Context Graph

## 9.1 Definition

The canonical context graph is the future ratified graph layer that determines current canonical context.

It should eventually contain:

```text
canonical nodes
canonical edges
authority class assignments
semantic identities
domain memberships
current source summaries
current workflow definitions
ratified role definitions
current graph-region ownership
```

## 9.2 Current status

```text
[PRODUCTION-GATED]
blocked until V36
```

## 9.3 Production rule

```text
No global canonical context graph write occurs until graph canon is ratified.
```

## 9.4 Required evidence before activation

```text
GRAPH_CANON_PROTOCOL.md
GRAPH_LAYER_REGISTRY.yaml
GRAPH_NODE_SCHEMA_REGISTRY.yaml
GRAPH_EDGE_SCHEMA_REGISTRY.yaml
GRAPH_WRITE_AUTHORITY_PROTOCOL.md
GRAPH_ROLLBACK_PROTOCOL.md
GRAPH_CONFLICT_AND_CONTRADICTION_PROTOCOL.md
tests for write authorization
tests for rollback
tests for conflict handling
tests for alias/truename handling
```

---

## 10. Release/Evidence Graph

## 10.1 Definition

The release/evidence graph tracks proof artifacts.

It contains:

```text
test outputs
certification reports
doctor reports
replay reports
evidence bundles
release candidates
checksums
verification reports
production-readiness reports
```

## 10.2 Current status

```text
[RUNTIME-PROVEN] in V29–V32 release-demo path
[A4/A2-candidate] after generalization
```

## 10.3 Production rule

```text
Release evidence proves what it declares; it does not automatically ratify runtime authority.
```

---

## 11. Agent Memory / Context Graph

## 11.1 Definition

The agent memory/context graph is the future graph layer used to distribute graph-region custody across agents and subagents.

It may contain:

```text
agent context packages
region assignments
leases
heartbeats
result receipts
fan-out packets
fan-in summaries
conflict reports
kill-switch events
```

## 11.2 Current status

```text
[PRODUCTION-GATED]
blocked until V39–V40
```

## 11.3 Production rule

```text
No agent or subagent receives autonomous context-region custody without activation law.
```

---

## 12. Graph Node Classes

Production graph canon should define node classes.

Initial candidate node classes:

```text
node.file
node.template
node.template_instance
node.packet
node.receipt
node.agent
node.role
node.domain
node.semantic_identity
node.summary
node.question
node.answer
node.event
node.reaction
node.proposal
node.review
node.commit
node.release_artifact
node.evidence_bundle
node.release_candidate
node.verification_report
node.production_readiness_report
node.context_package
node.lease
node.heartbeat
node.conflict
node.contradiction
node.rollback
```

Each node class requires:

```yaml
node_class:
  id:
  name:
  authority_class:
  allowed_layers: []
  required_fields: []
  optional_fields: []
  provenance_required: true
  receipt_required: true
  mutation_policy:
  promotion_policy:
```

---

## 13. Graph Edge Classes

Production graph canon should define edge classes.

Initial candidate edge classes:

```text
edge.instantiates
edge.derives_from
edge.references
edge.depends_on
edge.contradicts
edge.supersedes
edge.replaces
edge.proposes
edge.reviews
edge.commits
edge.rolls_back
edge.belongs_to_domain
edge.has_semantic_identity
edge.assigned_to_agent
edge.leased_to_agent
edge.spawned_by
edge.responds_to
edge.certifies
edge.verifies
edge.packages
edge.checksums
edge.blocks
edge.escalates
edge.settles
```

Each edge class requires:

```yaml
edge_class:
  id:
  name:
  source_node_classes: []
  target_node_classes: []
  allowed_layers: []
  authority_class:
  provenance_required: true
  reciprocal_required: false
  mutation_policy:
  promotion_policy:
```

---

## 14. Graph Region Registry

ION should use graph regions to avoid global context collapse.

Candidate regions:

```text
region.constitution
region.runtime_kernel
region.template_contracts
region.front_door
region.summary_refresh
region.release_evidence
region.production_readiness
region.graph_canon
region.source_summary_rewrite
region.agent_activation
region.daemon
region.product_surface
region.historical_lineage
```

Each region requires:

```yaml
graph_region:
  id:
  name:
  description:
  authority_class:
  owning_role:
  allowed_read_roles: []
  allowed_proposal_roles: []
  allowed_review_roles: []
  allowed_commit_roles: []
  canonical_write_allowed: false
  source_rewrite_allowed: false
  agent_activation_allowed: false
```

---

## 15. Graph Write Authority

Graph writes must be classified.

## 15.1 Write classes

```text
W0 read only
W1 working graph write
W2 proposal graph write
W3 review graph write
W4 bounded commit graph write
W5 canonical context graph write
W6 source graph rewrite
W7 agent memory/context graph activation write
```

## 15.2 Current permitted state

After V33 and before V36:

```text
W0 allowed
W1 allowed in bounded runtime contexts
W2 allowed where templates permit
W3 allowed where review surfaces permit
W4 allowed only in bounded demo/proven surfaces
W5 blocked
W6 blocked
W7 blocked
```

## 15.3 Production rule

```text
No W5, W6, or W7 write occurs before ratified authority exists.
```

---

## 16. Graph Promotion Path

A graph object should move through layers lawfully.

```text
working
→ proposal
→ review
→ bounded commit
→ canonical promotion
```

But not every object should reach canon.

Promotion requires:

```text
source provenance
schema validity
authority classification
contradiction scan
review verdict
receipt
rollback plan
```

Canonical promotion must also require graph-canon authority.

---

## 17. Graph Rollback

Rollback is not deletion.

Rollback means:

```text
record that a previous graph assertion is no longer current
preserve the historical node/edge
add a rollback edge or rollback node
restore prior canonical view where applicable
emit receipt
```

Rollback objects should include:

```yaml
rollback_record:
  rollback_id:
  target_node_or_edge:
  prior_state:
  restored_state:
  reason:
  reviewer:
  authority_class:
  receipt:
  timestamp:
```

Production rule:

```text
A graph mutation without rollback semantics is not production-safe.
```

---

## 18. Graph Migration

Graph migration is required when schemas, node classes, edge classes, or graph layers evolve.

Migration must be:

```text
planned
versioned
reviewed
receipted
rollback-capable
auditable
```

Migration record:

```yaml
graph_migration:
  migration_id:
  source_schema_version:
  target_schema_version:
  affected_layers: []
  affected_node_classes: []
  affected_edge_classes: []
  transformation_rules: []
  dry_run_report:
  review_verdict:
  commit_receipt:
  rollback_plan:
```

Production rule:

```text
No silent graph migration.
```

---

## 19. Conflict and Contradiction Handling

Graph canon must distinguish conflict from contradiction.

## 19.1 Conflict

A conflict occurs when two graph operations compete for the same surface.

Examples:

```text
two proposals modify the same summary
two agents claim the same region lease
two commits target the same bounded graph-state file
```

## 19.2 Contradiction

A contradiction occurs when two claims cannot both be true under the current authority model.

Examples:

```text
Codex is current orchestrator
Steward is current orchestrator
```

or:

```text
V10 is current runtime endpoint
V33 is current production-readiness frame
```

## 19.3 Required handling

```text
conflict -> lock, compare, merge, sequence, or reject
contradiction -> escalate, classify, settle, or preserve as historical split
```

## 19.4 Production rule

```text
Contradictions must not be smoothed into prose.
```

They must become graph objects or audit findings.

---

## 20. Alias and Truename Handling

ION’s history contains donor names, stale names, poetic names, and evolved truenames.

Graph canon must handle:

```text
historical aliases
current canonical names
deprecated names
blocked names
semantic collisions
role lineage names
file-system names
human-facing names
AI-facing names
```

Required alias record:

```yaml
semantic_alias_record:
  alias:
  canonical_name:
  alias_status:
    - CURRENT
    - HISTORICAL
    - DEPRECATED
    - BLOCKED
  source:
  rationale:
  valid_contexts: []
  invalid_contexts: []
  migration_required: true
```

Production rule:

```text
Historical alias does not outrank current truename.
```

This is especially important for:

```text
Codex
Seedsonnet
older donor-line authority labels
```

---

## 21. Graph Canon vs Source Summary Rewrite

Graph canon and source-summary rewrite are related but distinct.

Graph canon defines:

```text
what the canonical graph is
which graph layer may be written
how graph objects are promoted
how graph state rolls back
```

Source-summary rewrite defines:

```text
how canonical source summaries may be edited
how provenance is attached
how diffs are reviewed
how rollback restores text state
```

Production rule:

```text
Graph canon must exist before source-summary rewrite can safely commit into canonical context.
```

Therefore V36 should precede V37–V38.

---

## 22. Graph Canon vs Agent Activation

Agent activation depends on graph canon because agents operate graph regions.

Without graph canon, an agent cannot safely know:

```text
which region it owns
what it may read
what it may propose
what it may review
what it may commit
what it may not touch
how its results become graph objects
```

Production rule:

```text
Agent activation authority depends on graph-region authority.
```

Therefore V36 should precede V39–V40.

---

## 23. Graph Canon vs Daemon Runtime

The daemon executes graph reactions.

Without graph canon, a daemon may:

```text
watch the wrong surface
commit to the wrong layer
misclassify proposal as canon
replay stale events
overwrite bounded graph state
activate workflows without authority
```

Production rule:

```text
The production daemon must be graph-layer aware.
```

Therefore V36 should precede V41.

---

## 24. Proposed V36 Outputs

V36 should create:

```text
ION/02_architecture/GRAPH_CANON_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/GRAPH_LAYER_AND_WRITE_AUTHORITY_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/GRAPH_CONFLICT_AND_CONTRADICTION_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/GRAPH_MIGRATION_AND_ROLLBACK_PROTOCOL.md
ION/03_registry/graph_layer_registry.yaml
ION/03_registry/graph_node_class_registry.yaml
ION/03_registry/graph_edge_class_registry.yaml
ION/03_registry/graph_region_registry.yaml
ION/04_packages/kernel/graph_write_authority.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/graph_conflict_review.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/graph_rollback.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_graph_write_authority.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_graph_conflict_review.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_graph_rollback.py
```

---

## 25. Graph Canon Acceptance Criteria

Graph canon is minimally acceptable when:

```text
1. graph layers are defined
2. node classes are defined
3. edge classes are defined
4. graph regions are defined
5. write classes W0–W7 are defined
6. W5/W6/W7 are blocked by default
7. bounded commit remains distinct from canonical write
8. graph.py adapter status is clarified
9. alias/truename handling is defined
10. rollback semantics are defined
11. migration semantics are defined
12. conflict and contradiction handling are defined
13. tests prove unauthorized writes are refused
```

---

## 26. Anti-Patterns

## 26.1 Treating bounded commit as canon

Bad:

```text
V26 committed bounded graph state, therefore global graph canon exists.
```

Correct:

```text
V26 proved bounded graph-state commit. Global graph canon remains V36-gated.
```

## 26.2 Treating graph.py as the whole graph

Bad:

```text
graph.py is ION's living context graph.
```

Correct:

```text
graph.py is a runtime graph adapter or implementation surface; the living context graph is the system substrate.
```

## 26.3 Treating index projection as canon

Bad:

```text
The index says it, so it is canonical.
```

Correct:

```text
Index projection is a derived view and must be traced to graph/source authority.
```

## 26.4 Treating alias as authority

Bad:

```text
Seedsonnet was used historically, so it remains supreme authority.
```

Correct:

```text
Historical aliases are lineage evidence; current truenames require semantic ratification.
```

## 26.5 Treating working graph as committed graph

Bad:

```text
An agent's working graph state becomes project truth.
```

Correct:

```text
Working graph state must pass through proposal, review, and authorized commit/promotion.
```

---

## 27. Chapter Insert for Full Encyclopedia

## Chapter: Bounded Graph Commit Is Not Global Graph Canon

ION’s certified runtime path proves that a lawful template-instantiated file can become an evented graph object and eventually land in a bounded graph-state commit. This is a major proof. It means ION can move from document completion to graph action under validation and review.

But bounded graph commit is not global graph canon.

The bounded graph-state surface is deliberately limited. It lets ION act without pretending that every action has become canonical truth. This is one of ION’s most important safety properties. A proposal can exist. A review can land. A bounded commit can record a settlement. But none of those automatically rewrite the canonical context graph, canonical summaries, or source materials.

Production ION needs graph canon before it can claim canonical graph authority. Graph canon must define layers, node classes, edge classes, graph regions, write classes, rollback, migration, conflict handling, contradiction handling, and alias/truename promotion.

Until then, the correct claim is:

```text
ION has bounded evented graph-state commit.
ION does not yet have ratified global graph canon.
```

That boundary preserves the truth of the certified demo without overclaiming production authority.

---

## 28. Next Artifact

The next encyclopedia artifact should be:

```text
ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_SOURCE_SUMMARY_REWRITE_AUTHORITY_DRAFT.md
```

Purpose:

```text
define controlled source-summary rewrite authority, draft-vs-canonical summary distinction, provenance maps, diff/patch law, contradiction scans, review verdicts, bounded source-summary commit, and rollback receipts.
```


---

# Volume V — Source Summary Rewrite Authority

## 1. Why Source Summary Rewrite Is Dangerous

ION’s value depends on living context. If ION cannot update its own summaries, indexes, context packages, and explanatory surfaces, it becomes stale. But if ION updates them carelessly, it becomes untrustworthy.

Source-summary rewrite is dangerous because it can silently change the memory substrate of the system.

A source summary is not merely convenience prose. In ION, a source summary may influence:

```text
future retrieval
agent context packages
workflow routing
authority interpretation
graph projections
project continuity
what future agents believe happened
```

Therefore a model rewriting a summary is not just editing text. It may be changing the future operating memory of the project.

This is why the production rule is strict:

```text
No model may rewrite canonical source summaries directly.
```

All source-summary changes must pass through proposal, diff, provenance, contradiction scan, review, bounded commit, and rollback.

---

## 2. The Difference Between Summary Refresh and Source Summary Rewrite

The certified summary-refresh demo proves a bounded workflow path. It does not prove canonical source-summary rewrite authority.

The current certified path can do this:

```text
user request
→ summary-refresh template
→ event
→ reaction
→ projection
→ proposal
→ review
→ bounded graph-state commit
→ evidence
```

That is not the same as this:

```text
canonical source summary
→ edited canonical source summary
```

The production encyclopedia must preserve this difference.

## 2.1 Summary Refresh Demo

Status:

```text
[DEMO-PROVEN]
```

Rights:

```text
bounded graph-state evidence
proposal/review/commit inside bounded demo surface
no canonical source rewrite
```

## 2.2 Source Summary Rewrite Authority

Status:

```text
[PRODUCTION-GATED]
blocked until V37–V38
```

Rights after future ratification:

```text
draft summary generation
diff/patch proposal
provenance mapping
contradiction scanning
review verdict
bounded source-summary patch commit
rollback receipt
```

Production rule:

```text
A summary-refresh workflow may propose source-summary changes.
It may not apply them canonically until source-summary rewrite authority is ratified.
```

---

## 3. Summary Object Classes

Production ION should distinguish at least seven summary object classes.

```text
source material
source extract
draft summary
candidate summary
reviewed summary patch
canonical source summary
historical summary version
```

## 3.1 Source Material

Source material is the underlying artifact being summarized.

Examples:

```text
markdown document
protocol file
kernel module
registry YAML
test file
receipt
chat-derived doctrine packet
release report
historical donor document
```

Source material is not rewritten by a summary update.

## 3.2 Source Extract

A source extract is a bounded excerpt or structured extraction used to support a summary claim.

It may include:

```text
quoted passage
line reference
field reference
path reference
hash reference
semantic claim extraction
```

A source extract must preserve provenance.

## 3.3 Draft Summary

A draft summary is model-generated and non-canonical.

Rights:

```text
read
explain
proposal
```

Forbidden:

```text
canonical rewrite
source overwrite
future context promotion without review
```

## 3.4 Candidate Summary

A candidate summary is a draft summary that has passed formatting and schema validation and is ready for diff/review.

It is still not canonical.

## 3.5 Reviewed Summary Patch

A reviewed summary patch is a diff/patch object that has received a review verdict.

Possible verdicts:

```text
LAND
HOLD
ESCALATE
REJECT
NEEDS_SOURCE
NEEDS_CONTRADICTION_SCAN
NEEDS_HUMAN_REVIEW
```

## 3.6 Canonical Source Summary

A canonical source summary is the current accepted summary for a source or graph region.

It can influence future context.

Therefore it is protected.

## 3.7 Historical Summary Version

A historical summary version is a prior canonical summary preserved for rollback, audit, lineage, and contradiction analysis.

Production rule:

```text
Historical summaries are not deleted when replaced.
```

They are superseded, not erased.

---

## 4. Source Summary Rewrite Chain

The future production rewrite chain should be:

```text
source material
→ source extraction
→ draft summary
→ candidate summary
→ diff against current canonical summary
→ provenance map
→ contradiction scan
→ review verdict
→ source-summary patch proposal
→ bounded source-summary commit
→ rollback receipt
→ graph/index update proposal
```

Each arrow is a governed transformation.

No stage may be skipped when canonical summaries are affected.

---

## 5. Draft Summary Generation

Draft summary generation is the first model-authored step.

Inputs:

```text
source material
source extracts
current canonical summary if present
workflow goal
summary schema
authority class
target audience
```

Outputs:

```text
draft summary
claim list
source reference map
uncertainty list
omissions list
questions list
```

Draft summary rules:

```text
Drafts must not overwrite canonical summaries.
Drafts must identify missing source evidence.
Drafts must separate confident claims from inferred claims.
Drafts must record uncertainty.
Drafts must preserve contradictions rather than smoothing them.
```

Draft summary schema:

```yaml
draft_summary:
  draft_id:
  source_id:
  source_paths: []
  generated_at:
  generated_by:
  target_summary_id:
  summary_text:
  claims:
    - claim_id:
      claim_text:
      claim_status:
        - SOURCE_SUPPORTED
        - INFERRED
        - UNCERTAIN
        - CONTRADICTED
      source_refs: []
  omissions: []
  uncertainties: []
  open_questions: []
  forbidden_promotions:
    canonical_rewrite: true
```

---

## 6. Summary Diff and Patch

A summary rewrite must be expressed as a patch, not a silent replacement.

Patch types:

```text
add claim
remove claim
modify claim
split claim
merge claims
mark historical
mark contradicted
update terminology
update authority status
update runtime posture
```

Patch schema:

```yaml
summary_patch:
  patch_id:
  source_summary_id:
  target_summary_id:
  patch_type:
  old_text:
  new_text:
  rationale:
  affected_claims: []
  source_refs: []
  authority_effect:
    changes_authority_claim: false
    changes_runtime_posture: false
    changes_production_claim: false
  rollback_plan:
```

Production rule:

```text
No source-summary rewrite without a patch object.
```

---

## 7. Provenance Map

Every material summary claim must trace to provenance.

Provenance may include:

```text
file path
line range
hash
receipt
runtime report
test output
release artifact
human instruction
historical donor artifact
inference marker
```

Provenance record:

```yaml
provenance_record:
  provenance_id:
  claim_id:
  source_type:
    - file
    - line_range
    - receipt
    - runtime_report
    - test_output
    - release_artifact
    - human_instruction
    - historical_artifact
    - inference
  source_path:
  source_hash:
  line_range:
  excerpt:
  confidence:
  limitations:
```

Production rules:

```text
Claims affecting authority require explicit provenance.
Claims affecting production posture require explicit provenance.
Claims without provenance may remain as draft or question, not canon.
```

---

## 8. Contradiction Scan

Before a summary patch lands, ION must scan for contradictions.

Contradiction targets:

```text
authority class changes
role names
runtime posture
production readiness claims
graph canon claims
source rewrite claims
agent activation claims
historical/current name collisions
```

Example contradictions:

```text
V10 is the current runtime endpoint
V33 is the current production-readiness frame
```

or:

```text
Codex is current orchestrator
Steward is current orchestration truename
```

or:

```text
V32 proves production readiness
V32 proves certified demo baseline only
```

Contradiction scan schema:

```yaml
contradiction_scan:
  scan_id:
  patch_id:
  scanned_against:
    - current_summary
    - authority_registry
    - runtime_lineage
    - ratification_matrix
    - graph_canon
  contradictions_found:
    - contradiction_id:
      left_claim:
      right_claim:
      contradiction_type:
      severity:
      recommended_action:
  verdict:
    - CLEAR
    - HOLD
    - ESCALATE
```

Production rule:

```text
A contradiction scan with HOLD or ESCALATE blocks source-summary commit.
```

---

## 9. Review Verdict

Source-summary rewrite requires review.

Review verdicts:

```text
LAND
HOLD
ESCALATE
REJECT
NEEDS_SOURCE
NEEDS_CONTRADICTION_SCAN
NEEDS_HUMAN_REVIEW
```

Review record:

```yaml
summary_patch_review:
  review_id:
  patch_id:
  reviewer:
  reviewer_authority:
  verdict:
  rationale:
  required_changes: []
  blocked_claims: []
  approved_claims: []
  timestamp:
  receipt_required: true
```

Production rule:

```text
Only LAND may proceed to source-summary commit.
```

Even LAND must still obey write authority.

---

## 10. Source-Summary Commit

A source-summary commit is a controlled mutation to a canonical summary surface.

It requires:

```text
valid patch
provenance map
contradiction scan
LAND review verdict
write authority
rollback plan
receipt emission
```

Commit schema:

```yaml
source_summary_commit:
  commit_id:
  patch_id:
  target_summary_id:
  previous_summary_hash:
  new_summary_hash:
  reviewer:
  authority_class:
  committed_at:
  commit_scope:
    - summary_only
    - summary_and_index_update
    - summary_and_graph_update_proposal
  rollback_receipt:
  post_commit_checks: []
```

Production rule:

```text
A source-summary commit must be reversible.
```

---

## 11. Rollback Receipt

Rollback is mandatory.

A rollback receipt records how to reverse or supersede a summary mutation.

Rollback receipt schema:

```yaml
summary_rollback_receipt:
  rollback_id:
  commit_id:
  target_summary_id:
  previous_summary_hash:
  committed_summary_hash:
  restore_method:
    - restore_previous
    - supersede_with_patch
    - mark_invalid_and_revert
  rollback_preconditions:
  rollback_steps: []
  emitted_at:
  emitted_by:
```

Production rule:

```text
No rollback receipt, no source-summary commit.
```

---

## 12. Index and Graph Update After Summary Commit

A source-summary commit may require derived updates.

But these are separate operations:

```text
index projection update
graph projection update
canonical graph update proposal
context package refresh
agent context package invalidation
```

Production rule:

```text
A source-summary commit may trigger update proposals.
It does not automatically authorize global graph canon mutation.
```

This preserves the boundary from the graph canon draft.

---

## 13. Staleness Handling

Summaries become stale.

Staleness signals include:

```text
source hash changed
newer source material exists
contradiction discovered
role name changed
authority class changed
runtime posture changed
production readiness changed
test evidence changed
release candidate superseded
```

Staleness record:

```yaml
summary_staleness_record:
  staleness_id:
  summary_id:
  detected_at:
  reason:
  source_changes: []
  severity:
    - LOW
    - MEDIUM
    - HIGH
    - CRITICAL
  required_action:
    - refresh
    - audit
    - block_use
    - human_review
```

Production rule:

```text
A stale summary may remain historical, but must not be presented as current canon.
```

---

## 14. Summary Authority Classes

Not all summaries have the same authority.

| Summary class | Meaning | Rights |
|---|---|---|
| `DRAFT` | generated, unreviewed | read/proposal only |
| `CANDIDATE` | validated draft ready for review | proposal/review |
| `REVIEWED_HOLD` | reviewed but blocked | no commit |
| `REVIEWED_LAND` | approved patch | commit candidate |
| `CANONICAL` | current accepted source summary | protected |
| `HISTORICAL` | previous accepted summary | read/audit |
| `DEPRECATED` | invalid or replaced summary | historical only |
| `CONTRADICTED` | known contradiction | blocked from current use |

---

## 15. Source Summary Rewrite Permissions

Write classes:

```text
S0 read summary
S1 draft summary
S2 candidate summary
S3 propose patch
S4 review patch
S5 commit canonical summary patch
S6 rollback summary patch
S7 trigger graph/index update proposal
```

Current permitted state after V33:

```text
S0 allowed
S1 allowed in draft contexts
S2 allowed in proposal contexts
S3 allowed as proposal only
S4 allowed where review protocol exists
S5 blocked
S6 blocked
S7 proposal-only
```

After V37–V38, S5/S6 may be conditionally permitted under ratified authority.

Production rule:

```text
S5 and S6 require ratified source-summary rewrite authority.
```

---

## 16. Interaction with Production Graph Canon

Source-summary rewrite depends on graph canon.

Why:

```text
canonical summaries are graph-influencing context objects
summary changes may affect nodes, edges, roles, authority classes, and context packages
rollback requires graph-state awareness
contradiction scan requires graph comparisons
```

Therefore the order should be:

```text
V36 Graph Canon
→ V37 Source Summary Rewrite Proposal Authority
→ V38 Source Summary Rewrite Review + Bounded Commit
```

Production rule:

```text
No source-summary commit before graph canon establishes the relevant layer and write authority.
```

---

## 17. Interaction with Agents and Subagents

Agent/subagent systems depend on summaries.

If summaries are stale, agents inherit stale context. If summaries are silently rewritten, agents may inherit unreviewed doctrine.

Therefore source-summary rewrite must trigger:

```text
context package invalidation
agent context refresh proposal
lease review if active agents depend on changed summary
conflict alert if agent output used old summary
```

Production rule:

```text
Summary mutation must notify dependent context packages and active graph-region custodians.
```

This becomes essential after V39–V40.

---

## 18. Interaction with Release Engineering

A production release candidate must include summary rewrite evidence if summaries were changed.

Required evidence:

```text
summary patch reports
provenance maps
contradiction scans
review verdicts
commit receipts
rollback receipts
post-commit verification
```

Production rule:

```text
A release candidate that includes summary mutations must package summary rewrite evidence.
```

---

## 19. Proposed V37 Outputs

V37 should create proposal-only source-summary rewrite surfaces.

```text
ION/02_architecture/SOURCE_SUMMARY_REWRITE_AUTHORITY_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/SUMMARY_DIFF_AND_PATCH_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/SUMMARY_PROVENANCE_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/SUMMARY_STALENESS_AND_CONTRADICTION_PROTOCOL.md

ION/tests/test_kernel_source_summary_draft.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_summary_diff_patch.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_summary_provenance.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_summary_contradiction_scan.py
```

V37 should not permit canonical summary commit.

---

## 20. Proposed V38 Outputs

V38 should add reviewed bounded source-summary patch commit and rollback.

```text
ION/02_architecture/SOURCE_SUMMARY_PATCH_REVIEW_AND_COMMIT_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/SOURCE_SUMMARY_ROLLBACK_PROTOCOL.md
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_patch_review.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_patch_commit.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_rollback.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_dependent_context_invalidation.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_summary_patch_review.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_summary_patch_commit.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_summary_rollback.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_summary_dependent_context_invalidation.py
```

V38 may permit S5/S6 only inside explicitly bounded, reviewed, rollback-capable contexts.

---

## 21. Acceptance Criteria for Source Summary Rewrite Authority

Source-summary rewrite authority is minimally acceptable when:

```text
1. draft summaries cannot overwrite canonical summaries
2. all candidate summary patches have diffs
3. all material claims have provenance
4. contradiction scan blocks HOLD/ESCALATE cases
5. review verdict controls commit
6. LAND is required for commit
7. canonical summary commit records previous and new hash
8. rollback receipt is emitted
9. post-commit index/graph updates are proposals unless separately authorized
10. stale summaries can be marked stale or blocked from current use
11. source-summary changes can invalidate dependent context packages
12. unauthorized S5/S6 writes are refused by tests
```

---

## 22. Anti-Patterns

## 22.1 Direct rewrite

Bad:

```text
model opens canonical summary and edits it directly
```

Correct:

```text
model drafts patch, maps provenance, scans contradictions, receives review, commits with rollback
```

## 22.2 Summary laundering

Bad:

```text
unproven claim enters summary and becomes future context truth
```

Correct:

```text
unproven claim is tagged as inferred, uncertain, or blocked
```

## 22.3 Authority mutation by prose

Bad:

```text
summary update changes A3 to A2 without ratification
```

Correct:

```text
authority class changes require ratification record
```

## 22.4 Silent stale summary

Bad:

```text
old summary remains current after source changes
```

Correct:

```text
summary receives staleness record and refresh/audit task
```

## 22.5 Graph mutation smuggling

Bad:

```text
summary commit silently changes canonical graph nodes
```

Correct:

```text
summary commit may create graph update proposal, not automatic graph canon mutation
```

---

## 23. Chapter Insert for Full Encyclopedia

## Chapter: No Model May Rewrite Canonical Summaries Directly

ION’s future depends on living self-documentation. If the system cannot update its own summaries, it will eventually lose contact with its current state. But if it updates summaries casually, it will corrupt the very memory substrate it depends on.

A canonical source summary is not just prose. It is a future-context surface. It influences what agents retrieve, what workflows believe, how graph regions are understood, what authority posture is remembered, and what a future continuation packet may treat as true.

Therefore a model must never rewrite a canonical source summary directly.

The lawful path is longer:

```text
draft summary
→ diff
→ provenance map
→ contradiction scan
→ review verdict
→ bounded patch commit
→ rollback receipt
```

This path is not bureaucracy. It is the mechanism by which ION prevents self-documentation from becoming self-corruption.

The current certified summary-refresh demo proves that summary-related workflows can move through an evented graph chain and land bounded graph-state evidence. It does not prove canonical source-summary rewrite authority.

The correct current claim is:

```text
ION has certified a bounded summary-refresh demo path.
ION has not yet ratified source-summary rewrite authority.
```

That boundary keeps ION honest enough to become production-ready.

---

## 24. Next Artifact

The next encyclopedia artifact should be:

```text
ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_AGENT_SUBAGENT_ARCHITECTURE_DRAFT.md
```

Purpose:

```text
define agent/subagent graph operations, contextual node workers, domain manager agents, fan-out/fan-in orchestration, agent context packages, leases, heartbeats, result receipts, conflict escalation, and kill-switch law.
```
