## 24. V42 Acceptance Criteria

The production front door is minimally production-candidate when:

```text
1. Persona Interface, Relay, and Steward remain distinct.
2. CLI can show readiness, verify releases, and inspect doctor/certification reports.
3. API requests carry idempotency keys and authority claims.
4. review queue is visible.
5. artifact browser can locate receipts/reports/release candidates.
6. response packages include authority used and boundaries not crossed.
7. refusal packages are explicit.
8. operator trace is generated for front-door actions.
9. front door cannot bypass daemon locks.
10. front door cannot rewrite summaries directly.
11. front door cannot spawn agents before activation law.
12. front door cannot claim production readiness while readiness verdict is negative.
```

---

## 25. Anti-Patterns

## 25.1 Chat as authority

Bad:

```text
the user asked in chat, so ION did it
```

Correct:

```text
chat request becomes graph-native packet and follows authority gates
```

## 25.2 Friendly overclaim

Bad:

```text
Great news, ION is basically production-ready!
```

Correct:

```text
ION has certified demo baseline and production-readiness gate; production verdict remains NOT_PRODUCTION_READY.
```

## 25.3 Invisible refusal

Bad:

```text
request silently does nothing because blocked
```

Correct:

```text
front door returns refusal package with gate and next lawful move
```

## 25.4 UI bypass

Bad:

```text
operator dashboard button directly mutates graph
```

Correct:

```text
button creates authorized workflow request and trace
```

## 25.5 Artifact obscurity

Bad:

```text
evidence exists somewhere in history folders
```

Correct:

```text
artifact browser exposes evidence by type, status, hash, and relation
```

---

## 26. Chapter Insert for Full Encyclopedia

## Chapter: The Front Door Is Governance Made Visible

ION’s front door is not just a chat interface. It is the user-visible edge of a governed living context graph.

A user should not have to understand every internal protocol to use ION, but ION must not hide its authority boundaries behind friendly language. If a request is blocked because source-summary rewrite authority is not ratified, the front door should say that. If a release candidate is verified only as a demo release candidate, the front door should say that. If the daemon is in safe mode, the front door should say that. If review is required, the front door should surface the review queue.

The front door has three central roles. Persona Interface renders user-facing meaning. Relay translates across the semantic boundary. Steward routes graph-native work. Together they prevent one overloaded “assistant” from becoming user persona, translator, orchestrator, reviewer, daemon, and authority all at once.

The front door does not bypass ION’s law. It reveals it.

The current correct claim is:

```text
ION has a front-door demo spine.
ION has not yet ratified the full production front-door product surface.
```

---

## 27. Next Artifact

The next encyclopedia artifact should be:

```text
ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_RELEASE_ENGINEERING_AND_VERIFICATION_DRAFT.md
```

Purpose:

```text
define release/evidence engineering, evidence bundles, release-candidate capsules, verifiers, production release candidates, tamper audits, operator handoff, and why verified demo release candidates are not production releases.
```


---

# Volume IX — Release Engineering and Verification

## 1. Why Release Engineering Matters

ION is a continuity system. Therefore its releases are not mere zip files.

A release artifact in ION must be able to answer:

```text
What exactly is included?
What source state produced it?
What tests passed?
What reports exist?
What evidence supports the claim?
What boundaries are declared?
What is certified?
What is not certified?
What is verified?
What is not production-ready?
What can an operator reproduce?
What changed since the previous release?
What hashes prove integrity?
```

Without this, ION’s continuity artifacts become ordinary archives, and ordinary archives are not enough. ION’s release engineering must preserve graph continuity, authority posture, evidence, proof, boundaries, and recoverability.

Release engineering is the product-facing expression of ION’s proof discipline.

---

## 2. Current Release Lineage

The release/evidence lineage currently runs:

```text
V27 replay CLI
→ V28 replay doctor
→ V29 certification gate
→ V30 evidence bundle
→ V31 release-candidate capsule
→ V32 release-candidate verifier
→ V33 production-readiness charter
```

Short form:

```text
replay → doctor → certify → bundle evidence → package release candidate → verify capsule → report production readiness
```

This lineage proves that ION can package and verify a certified demo release candidate.

It does not prove production release readiness.

---

## 3. Release Classes

Production ION should distinguish at least seven release classes.

| Class | Meaning | Production implication |
|---|---|---|
| `DEMO_RUN` | local workflow run | not a release |
| `DEMO_EVIDENCE_BUNDLE` | packaged evidence for a demo workflow | proof bundle, not release candidate by itself |
| `DEMO_RELEASE_CANDIDATE` | checksummed capsule for demo handoff | verified demo artifact |
| `CERTIFIED_DEMO_BASELINE` | verified demo RC accepted as baseline | V32 role |
| `PRODUCTION_READINESS_REPORT` | report of remaining production gates | V33 role |
| `PRODUCTION_RELEASE_CANDIDATE` | future production-scoped release candidate | blocked until V44 |
| `VERIFIED_PRODUCTION_RELEASE` | future independently verified production release | blocked until V45 |

Production rule:

```text
A release artifact must declare its release class.
```

---

## 4. Evidence Bundle

## 4.1 Definition

An evidence bundle packages proof artifacts for a workflow or release claim.

Evidence bundle contents may include:

```text
certification report
doctor report
replay reports
readiness report
test output
operator command list
boundary statement
manifest
README
```

## 4.2 Current implementation status

The V30 evidence bundle is demo-scoped and summary-refresh-specific.

Current class:

```text
[A4-DEMO] / [RUNTIME-PROVEN]
```

Production target:

```text
generic evidence_bundle_builder.py after V35
```

## 4.3 Evidence bundle rule

```text
Evidence bundles package proof; they do not create authority.
```

A bundle can prove that declared evidence exists. It cannot ratify a provisional surface by itself.

---

## 5. Certification Report

## 5.1 Definition

A certification report converts evidence into a declared verdict.

Current V29 verdicts:

```text
CERTIFIED
BLOCKED
```

## 5.2 Certification scope

A certification report must declare its scope.

Examples:

```text
summary-refresh demo certified
release candidate verified
production readiness not ready
source-summary rewrite blocked
```

## 5.3 Certification rule

```text
CERTIFIED means declared evidence requirements passed within declared scope.
```

It does not mean:

```text
production-ready
ratified
globally canonical
safe for all workflows
```

---

## 6. Release Candidate Capsule

## 6.1 Definition

A release-candidate capsule is a portable, reviewable, checksummed package.

Current V31 demo capsule contents:

```text
summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate_manifest.json
README.md
COMMANDS.sh
CHECKSUMS.sha256
evidence_bundle/
```

## 6.2 Required production capsule contents

A future production release candidate should include:

```text
production_release_candidate_manifest.json
README.md
COMMANDS.sh
CHECKSUMS.sha256
PRODUCTION_EVIDENCE_BUNDLE/
PRODUCTION_READINESS_REPORT.json
RATIFICATION_REPORTS/
GRAPH_CANON_REPORT/
SOURCE_SUMMARY_REWRITE_REPORT/
AGENT_ACTIVATION_REPORT/
DAEMON_SAFETY_REPORT/
ADVERSARIAL_AUDIT_REPORTS/
OPERATOR_HANDOFF.md
KNOWN_BOUNDARIES.md
```

## 6.3 Release candidate rule

```text
A release candidate is a candidate, not a release.
```

It becomes verified only after independent verification.

---

## 7. Release Candidate Manifest

A release-candidate manifest should declare:

```yaml
release_candidate_manifest:
  release_candidate_id:
  release_class:
    - DEMO_RELEASE_CANDIDATE
    - PRODUCTION_RELEASE_CANDIDATE
  emitted_at:
  source_artifact:
  source_artifact_hash:
  included_paths: []
  evidence_bundle:
  commands_path:
  checksums_path:
  readiness_verdict:
  certification_verdict:
  verification_status:
  production_claim: false
  boundaries:
    production_ready_claimed:
    canonical_graph_write_authorized:
    source_summary_rewrite_authorized:
    agent_activation_authorized:
    daemon_production_authorized:
  required_verifier:
```

Production rule:

```text
The manifest is the release candidate’s claim surface.
```

Every release claim must be manifest-visible.

---

## 8. Checksums

Checksums provide integrity, not meaning.

A checksum can prove:

```text
this file matches the file that was hashed
```

A checksum cannot prove:

```text
the file is correct
the file is ratified
the file is production-ready
```

Production rule:

```text
Checksums prove integrity, not authority.
```

Release verification requires both:

```text
checksum validation
claim validation
```

---

## 9. Verifier

## 9.1 Definition

A verifier independently checks an existing release-candidate capsule.

V32 verifies:

```text
release candidate directory exists
manifest JSON exists/readable
verdict/certified status valid
README exists
COMMANDS exists
CHECKSUMS exists
copied evidence_bundle exists
checksums match
required commands present
forbidden boundary claims remain false
```

## 9.2 Verifier rule

```text
The verifier checks the package; it does not rerun all production work.
```

It may verify package integrity and declared evidence. It does not replace the underlying tests, audits, or ratification reports.

## 9.3 Demo verifier vs production verifier

Current:

```text
V32 = demo release-candidate verifier
```

Future:

```text
V45 = production release-candidate verifier
```

Production rule:

```text
A verified demo RC is not a verified production release.
```

---

## 10. Production Readiness Report

A production-readiness report is not a release candidate.

It reports whether production gates are closed.

Current V33 verdict:

```text
NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
```

A production release candidate may not override a readiness report.

Production rule:

```text
If production-readiness verdict is negative, production release is blocked.
```

---

## 11. Tamper Audit

A tamper audit tests whether release artifacts have been altered, mismatched, or misrepresented.

Tamper targets:

```text
manifest mismatch
checksum mismatch
missing evidence bundle
missing report
stale certification
wrong release class
boundary claim altered
production-ready claim inserted
historical artifact substituted
path collision
duplicate release candidate ID
```

Tamper audit record:

```yaml
release_tamper_audit:
  audit_id:
  release_candidate_id:
  checked_files:
  checksum_mismatches: []
  missing_files: []
  manifest_conflicts: []
  boundary_claim_conflicts: []
  stale_reports: []
  verdict:
    - CLEAN
    - FAILED
    - ESCALATE
```

Production rule:

```text
Tamper audit failure blocks release verification.
```

---

## 12. Operator Handoff

Operator handoff is the human-facing release explanation.

It should include:

```text
what this artifact is
what it proves
what it does not prove
how to verify it
how to reproduce key checks
what commands to run
what reports to inspect
what boundaries remain
what next action is lawful
```

Operator handoff is mandatory because release artifacts must be usable outside the generating chat or agent.

Production rule:

```text
A release candidate without operator handoff is incomplete.
```

---

## 13. Boundary Statement

Every release candidate must include explicit boundary claims.

Demo release boundary example:

```yaml
boundaries:
  production_ready_claimed: false
  global_graph_canon_claimed: false
  source_summary_rewrite_authorized: false
  agent_activation_authorized: false
  daemon_production_authorized: false
  constitutional_ratification_claimed: false
```

Production release boundary example, if future gates pass:

```yaml
boundaries:
  production_ready_claimed: true
  production_ready_verification_report:
  global_graph_canon_report:
  source_summary_rewrite_authority_report:
  agent_activation_authority_report:
  daemon_safety_report:
  adversarial_audit_report:
```

Production rule:

```text
Release boundaries must be machine-readable.
```

---

## 14. Release Evidence Graph

Release engineering should eventually be represented in the release/evidence graph.

Candidate node classes:

```text
node.replay_report
node.doctor_report
node.certification_report
node.evidence_bundle
node.release_candidate
node.checksum_file
node.verification_report
node.production_readiness_report
node.tamper_audit
node.operator_handoff
```

Candidate edge classes:

```text
edge.certifies
edge.packages
edge.includes
edge.checksums
edge.verifies
edge.blocks
edge.supersedes
edge.depends_on
edge.references
```

Production rule:

```text
Release artifacts should be graph-navigable.
```

---

## 15. Release Supersession

Releases are superseded, not erased.

Supersession record:

```yaml
release_supersession:
  supersession_id:
  old_release_candidate:
  new_release_candidate:
  reason:
  compatibility:
    - compatible
    - incompatible
    - security_fix
    - evidence_update
    - boundary_change
  old_status:
    - superseded
    - revoked
    - historical
  emitted_at:
```

Production rule:

```text
A superseded release remains historical evidence.
```

---

## 16. Revocation

A release candidate may be revoked.

Revocation triggers:

```text
checksum mismatch
missing evidence
false production claim
critical audit finding
unsafe mutation discovered
stale authority discovered
wrong source artifact
operator error
```

Revocation record:

```yaml
release_revocation:
  revocation_id:
  release_candidate_id:
  reason:
  severity:
  revoked_by:
  revoked_at:
  replacement:
  operator_notice_required: true
```

Production rule:

```text
A revoked release must remain visible as revoked.
```

---

## 17. Reproducibility

Release engineering should maximize reproducibility.

A release candidate should include:

```text
commands
environment assumptions
source artifact hash
test command list
verification command
expected verdicts
known skipped tests
known boundaries
```

Production rule:

```text
A future operator should be able to verify the release without chat history.
```

---

## 18. Release Command Families

Current command families should generalize into:

```bash
ion workflow replay --workflow <id>
ion workflow doctor --workflow <id>
ion workflow certify --workflow <id>
ion evidence bundle --workflow <id>
ion release candidate --workflow <id>
ion release verify --candidate <id>
ion readiness production
ion release tamper-audit --candidate <id>
```

Production release commands should be separate:

```bash
ion production candidate
ion production verify
ion production handoff
```

Production rule:

```text
Demo release commands and production release commands must not be ambiguous.
```

---

## 19. V44 Production Release Candidate

V44 should create the first production release candidate only after V34–V43 gates pass.

Required inputs:

```text
A3 ratification report
demo/production primitive split report
graph canon report
source-summary rewrite authority report
agent activation authority report
daemon safety report
front-door product surface report
adversarial production audit report
production readiness report
```

Required outputs:

```text
ION_PRODUCTION_RELEASE_CANDIDATE_<date>.zip
PRODUCTION_RELEASE_CANDIDATE_MANIFEST.json
PRODUCTION_EVIDENCE_BUNDLE/
OPERATOR_HANDOFF.md
KNOWN_BOUNDARIES.md
CHECKSUMS.sha256
COMMANDS.sh
```

Production rule:

```text
No V44 production release candidate while critical production gates remain open.
```

---

## 20. V45 Production Verifier

V45 should independently verify the production release candidate.

Verifier checks:

```text
manifest valid
release class is PRODUCTION_RELEASE_CANDIDATE
checksums valid
evidence bundle exists
all required production reports exist
readiness verdict is READY/PRODUCTION_READY
critical audits clean
boundary claims consistent
commands present
operator handoff present
supersession/revocation status clean
```

Production verifier verdicts:

```text
VERIFIED_PRODUCTION_RELEASE
FAILED
BLOCKED
ESCALATE
```

Production rule:

```text
Production is not claimed until the production verifier passes.
```

---

## 21. Production Release Acceptance Criteria

A production release may be claimed only when:

```text
1. release candidate class is PRODUCTION_RELEASE_CANDIDATE
2. production readiness verdict is positive
3. A3 surface ratification complete
4. demo/production primitive split complete
5. graph canon ratified
6. source-summary rewrite authority governed
7. agent activation authority governed
8. daemon safety proven
9. front-door product surface tested
10. adversarial audit critical blockers = zero
11. evidence bundle complete
12. checksums valid
13. production verifier passes
14. operator handoff complete
```

---

## 22. Anti-Patterns

## 22.1 Verified demo = production

Bad:

```text
V32 verified the release candidate, so ION is production-ready.
```

Correct:

```text
V32 verified the demo release candidate. Production readiness remains blocked until future gates pass.
```

## 22.2 Checksum = correctness

Bad:

```text
checksum matches, so release is correct.
```

Correct:

```text
checksum matches file integrity; correctness requires evidence and verification.
```

## 22.3 Release without boundary

Bad:

```text
zip file delivered with no boundary claims.
```

Correct:

```text
release candidate includes machine-readable boundaries.
```

## 22.4 Hidden evidence

Bad:

```text
tests passed somewhere in chat.
```

Correct:

```text
test outputs and reports are packaged in evidence bundle.
```

## 22.5 Production label without verifier

Bad:

```text
call a zip production because the builder believes it is ready.
```

Correct:

```text
production release requires production verifier.
```

---

## 23. Chapter Insert for Full Encyclopedia

## Chapter: A Release Zip Is Not Enough

ION’s release artifact is not merely a compressed folder. It is a continuity capsule. A release must carry the evidence needed for another agent, operator, or future version of ION to understand what it is, what it proves, what it does not prove, and how to verify it.

The V32 certified demo baseline is important because it proves that a demo release candidate can be packaged and independently verified. That release candidate contains a manifest, commands, checksums, evidence bundle, and boundary statement. The verifier checks that the capsule is structurally intact, checksum-consistent, certified, evidence-backed, and honest about forbidden production claims.

But a verified demo release candidate is not a production release.

Production release engineering requires more: ratification reports, graph canon evidence, source-summary rewrite authority evidence, agent activation authority evidence, daemon safety evidence, front-door product evidence, adversarial audit evidence, and a production verifier. Without those, a release may be valuable, but it is not production.

The correct current claim is:

```text
ION has verified demo release engineering.
ION does not yet have a verified production release.
```

---

## 24. Next Artifact

The next encyclopedia artifact should be:

```text
ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_BUILDER_IMPLEMENTATION_GUIDE_DRAFT.md
```

Purpose:

```text
define builder reconstruction tracks, implementation order, required files, command families, test matrix, migration from V33 to production, and how an AI builder can rebuild ION without hidden oral context.
```


---

# Volume X — Builder Implementation Guide

## 1. Purpose of the Builder Guide

The production encyclopedia must be more than an explanation. It must be able to function as a reconstruction guide.

A future AI builder should be able to read the encyclopedia and answer:

```text
What is ION?
What is the smallest correct version of ION?
What is the certified demo baseline?
What is the production-readiness posture?
What files and protocols are required?
What order should implementation follow?
What tests prove each stage?
What claims remain blocked?
How do I avoid repeating historical drift?
```

The builder guide exists to prevent future agents from rediscovering ION by accident, flattening its law into a README, or prematurely calling a demo path production.

---

## 2. Reconstruction Tracks

Different builders need different reconstruction depths.

The production encyclopedia should define six tracks.

```text
Track A — Conceptual Reconstruction
Track B — Kernel-Only Reconstruction
Track C — Evented Template Runtime Reconstruction
Track D — Front-Door Product Reconstruction
Track E — Certified Release-Demo Reconstruction
Track F — Full Production Reconstruction
```

Each track has different required surfaces and acceptance criteria.

---

## 3. Track A — Conceptual Reconstruction

## 3.1 Purpose

Track A reconstructs ION as a coherent idea.

It is for:

```text
new human readers
new AI agents
investor/product explanation
architectural orientation
doctrine review
```

## 3.2 Required concepts

```text
living context graph
lawful agents
templates
packets
receipts
registries
bounded context
evented template file graph
front-door split
production-readiness posture
```

## 3.3 Minimal correct sentence

```text
ION lets AI agents remember, coordinate, and evolve complex work by turning context into a governed living graph.
```

## 3.4 Acceptance criteria

Track A is successful if the builder can explain:

```text
1. why ION is not just memory/RAG
2. why ION is not just a chatbot
3. why files become graph objects
4. why templates create lawful event pressure
5. why V32 is certified demo baseline
6. why V33 is NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
7. why production readiness requires ratification
```

Track A does not require code.

---

## 4. Track B — Kernel-Only Reconstruction

## 4.1 Purpose

Track B reconstructs the minimum kernel model.

It is for:

```text
runtime architects
test authors
kernel module builders
agents preparing implementation packets
```

## 4.2 Required kernel concepts

```text
store
index
graph
context compiler
template contract validator
event extractor
reaction selector
projection writer
proposal writer
review handler
bounded commit handler
receipt writer
release readiness gate
```

## 4.3 Required directories

```text
ION/02_architecture/
ION/03_registry/
ION/04_packages/kernel/
ION/05_context/
ION/07_templates/
ION/tests/
```

## 4.4 Required kernel files or future equivalents

```text
kernel/graph.py
kernel/context_compiler.py
kernel/template_metadata_contracts.py
kernel/template_completion_events.py
kernel/template_reaction_selection.py
kernel/template_index_projection.py
kernel/template_graph_writeback.py
kernel/release_readiness.py
```

## 4.5 Acceptance criteria

Track B is successful if:

```text
1. templates can be validated against contracts
2. completion events can be created
3. reactions can be selected
4. projection-only surfaces remain projection-only
5. proposal-only surfaces remain proposal-only
6. review is required before bounded commit
7. bounded commit cannot overwrite existing state silently
8. receipts are emitted
```

Track B does not require front-door productization.

---

## 5. Track C — Evented Template Runtime Reconstruction

## 5.1 Purpose

Track C reconstructs the V10/V26 evented template runtime line.

It is for:

```text
workflow runtime builders
template automation builders
graph-state commit validators
```

## 5.2 Required path

```text
template instance
→ completion event
→ reaction selection
→ index projection
→ graph write proposal
→ review verdict
→ bounded graph-state commit
→ receipt
```

## 5.3 Required tests

```text
test_template_metadata_contracts
test_template_completion_events
test_template_reaction_selection
test_template_index_projection
test_template_graph_writeback_proposal
test_template_graph_writeback_review
test_template_graph_commit
```

## 5.4 Acceptance criteria

Track C is successful if:

```text
1. invalid template cannot emit valid completion event
2. missing contract blocks event
3. reaction must be allowed by contract
4. projection cannot become canonical graph write
5. proposal cannot commit without review
6. HOLD blocks commit
7. LAND permits bounded commit only
8. duplicate commit is refused or idempotently resolved
```

Track C does not prove production graph canon.

---

## 6. Track D — Front-Door Product Reconstruction

## 6.1 Purpose

Track D reconstructs the product-facing intake/return path.

It is for:

```text
chat product builders
API builders
CLI builders
operator dashboard designers
front-door protocol authors
```

## 6.2 Required chain

```text
User / External Caller
→ Persona Interface
→ Relay
→ Steward
→ workflow/daemon/review/release surface
→ Steward return
→ Relay return package
→ Persona Interface response
→ User / External Caller
```

## 6.3 Required surfaces

```text
FRONT_DOOR_PERSONA_RELAY_STEWARD_BOUNDARY_PROTOCOL.md
FRONT_DOOR_RUNTIME_ENTRY_PROTOCOL.md
FRONT_DOOR_CHAT_ORCHESTRATION_ADAPTER_PROTOCOL.md
ROLE_MIXING_AND_ROLE_SPLIT_GUARD_PROTOCOL.md
PERSONA_INTERFACE.boot.md
PERSONA_INTERFACE.semantic.yaml
RELAY__SEMANTIC_BOUNDARY.md
PERSONA_INTERFACE__USER_RESPONSE.md
```

## 6.4 Acceptance criteria

Track D is successful if:

```text
1. Persona Interface, Relay, and Steward remain distinct
2. user input becomes graph-native packet
3. graph-native result becomes user response package
4. front door cannot bypass authority checks
5. response package includes boundaries and artifacts
6. refusals are explicit
7. production readiness cannot be overclaimed
```

Track D does not prove daemon production safety.

---

## 7. Track E — Certified Release-Demo Reconstruction

## 7.1 Purpose

Track E reconstructs the V26–V32 certified summary-refresh release-demo spine.

It is for:

```text
demo/release engineers
operator handoff builders
verification authors
continuation agents
```

## 7.2 Required path

```text
summary-refresh bounded commit demo
→ replay CLI
→ replay doctor
→ certification gate
→ evidence bundle
→ release-candidate capsule
→ release-candidate verifier
```

## 7.3 Required commands

```bash
PYTHONPATH=ION/04_packages python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_replay --workspace-root .
PYTHONPATH=ION/04_packages python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_doctor --workspace-root .
PYTHONPATH=ION/04_packages python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_certification --workspace-root .
PYTHONPATH=ION/04_packages python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_evidence_bundle --workspace-root .
PYTHONPATH=ION/04_packages python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate --workspace-root .
PYTHONPATH=ION/04_packages python -S -m kernel.summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate_verify --workspace-root .
```

## 7.4 Acceptance criteria

Track E is successful if:

```text
1. project-root smoke can run safely
2. isolated full commit can land bounded graph-state
3. certification reports CERTIFIED within declared scope
4. evidence bundle contains reports
5. release candidate contains manifest, README, commands, checksums, evidence
6. verifier reports VERIFIED
7. forbidden boundary claims remain false
8. production readiness is not claimed
```

Track E proves certified demo baseline, not production readiness.

---

## 8. Track F — Full Production Reconstruction

## 8.1 Purpose

Track F reconstructs production ION.

It is for:

```text
full-system builders
production-release candidates
multi-agent runtime builders
daemon implementers
release verifiers
```

## 8.2 Required gates

```text
V34 A3 Surface Ratification Pass
V35 Demo/Production Primitive Split
V36 Global Graph Canon
V37 Source Summary Rewrite Proposal Authority
V38 Source Summary Rewrite Review + Commit
V39 Agent Activation Authority
V40 Subagent Fan-Out/Fan-In Runtime
V41 Production Daemon Runtime Loop
V42 Production Front-Door CLI/API
V43 Adversarial Production Audit
V44 Production Release Candidate
V45 Production Verifier
```

## 8.3 Acceptance criteria

Track F is successful only if:

```text
1. all production surfaces are ratified
2. demo wrappers are separated from primitives
3. graph canon is ratified
4. source-summary rewrite is governed and reversible
5. agent activation is leased, receipted, and kill-switchable
6. daemon is idempotent, queue-locked, safe-mode capable, and recoverable
7. front door exposes traceability, refusal UX, review queue, artifacts
8. adversarial audit has zero critical blockers
9. production release candidate is packaged
10. production verifier passes
```

Track F is the only track that may claim production readiness.

---

## 9. Canonical Build Order

A future builder should follow this order.

```text
1. Preserve source authority ledger.
2. Preserve root invariant.
3. Reframe V10 as milestone.
4. Lock V32 as certified demo baseline.
5. Lock V33 as NOT_PRODUCTION_READY posture.
6. Build/verify ratification matrix.
7. Split demo surfaces from production primitives.
8. Ratify graph canon.
9. Implement source-summary rewrite proposal/review/commit.
10. Implement agent activation authority.
11. Implement bounded subagent fan-out/fan-in.
12. Implement daemon runtime safety.
13. Implement production front-door surfaces.
14. Run adversarial production audit.
15. Package production release candidate.
16. Verify production release candidate.
```

The order matters because later gates depend on earlier gates.

---

```text
ION/
  00_BOOTSTRAP/
  01_law/

    kernel/
  05_context/

    summaries/

  07_templates/
  agents/
  tests/
```

The exact folder names may evolve, but the functional surfaces must remain.

## 14. Migration from V33 to Production

The migration path from V33 is:

```text
V33 = readiness gate exists
V34 = classify surfaces
V35 = extract primitives
V36 = ratify graph canon
V37 = source-summary rewrite proposal
V38 = source-summary commit/rollback
V39 = agent activation protocol
V40 = subagent runtime
V41 = daemon safety
V42 = product front door
V43 = adversarial audit
V44 = production release candidate
V45 = production verifier
```

A builder should not skip directly from V33 to production packaging.

---

## 15. Implementation Packet Pattern

Every major build pass should produce:

```text
protocol document
template/report document
kernel/module code where applicable
tests
registry update where applicable
task packet
receipt
changelog
manifest
zip artifact
```

Minimum packet schema:

```yaml
implementation_packet:
  packet_id:
  date:
  base_artifact:
  objective:
  authority_posture:
  created_surfaces: []
  modified_surfaces: []
  tests: []
  receipts: []
  boundaries:
    production_claim: false
    canonical_write_authorized: false
    source_rewrite_authorized: false
    agent_activation_authorized: false
  next_lawful_move:
```

---

## 16. Builder Anti-Drift Rules

## 16.1 Do not trust smoothness

If a document sounds coherent but lacks evidence, it is not enough.

## 16.2 Do not promote demo surfaces by renaming

A demo wrapper renamed as a primitive is still a demo wrapper if assumptions remain.

## 16.3 Do not erase history

Historical donor names and stale names must be mapped, not silently deleted.

## 16.4 Do not resurrect stale authority

Codex is historical-only in the current authority frame.

## 16.5 Do not rewrite summaries directly

Source-summary rewrite remains blocked until V37–V38 authority.

## 16.6 Do not call bounded graph-state commit graph canon

Bounded commit is not canonical graph write.

## 16.7 Do not let a daemon become law

Daemon executes authorized reactions; it does not create authority.

## 16.8 Do not let agents become truth

Agent outputs are claims with receipts, not canon.

## 16.9 Do not hide refusal

Blocked action must be visible.

## 16.10 Do not claim production readiness before verifier

Production readiness requires production release candidate and production verifier.

---

## 17. Minimal Rebuild From Zero

If rebuilding from zero, the minimum lawful order is:

```text
1. create filesystem skeleton
2. write source authority ledger
3. write root invariant and claims ledger
4. create template contract schema
5. create template completion event
6. create reaction selection
7. create projection/proposal/review/commit surfaces
8. create bounded graph-state commit tests
9. create front-door Persona/Relay/Steward adapter
10. create summary-refresh demo workflow
11. create replay/doctor/certification/evidence/release/verifier
12. create production readiness gate
13. freeze certified demo baseline
14. begin production ratification path
```

This produces the V33-equivalent foundation, not production.

---

## 18. Production Rebuild From V33

If starting from V33, do not rebuild everything.

Instead:

```text
1. verify V32/V33 artifacts
2. run production_readiness.py
3. confirm NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
4. run ratification matrix draft
5. implement V34 surface classification
6. continue V35–V45
```

Production rebuild from V33 should preserve all V26–V32 evidence.

## 20. Builder Evidence Discipline

Every builder claim should be backed by one of:

```text
file path
test output
receipt
manifest hash
release candidate
verification report
source reference
ratification record
```

Forbidden phrase pattern:

```text
It seems production-ready.
```

Required phrase pattern:

```text
This passes declared checks X/Y under boundary Z and does not prove A/B/C.
```

---

## 21. How an AI Builder Should Use the Encyclopedia

An AI builder should treat the encyclopedia as:

```text
context
map
doctrine
build sequence
claim discipline
```

Not as:

```text
automatic permission
production verifier
mutation authority
source of hidden truth
```

AI builder workflow:

```text
read source ledger
identify target track
load relevant part
create bounded task packet
state authority posture
perform work
emit receipt
emit tests
emit manifest
state boundaries
package artifact
```

---

## 22. How a Human Builder Should Use the Encyclopedia

A human builder should use the encyclopedia to:

```text
understand ION’s shape
choose next production gate
review AI outputs
detect overclaims
inspect artifacts
verify release status
guide implementation priorities
```

Human review questions:

```text
What claim is being made?
What class is the surface?
What evidence supports it?
What mutation rights are requested?
What remains blocked?
Is the output preserving V32/V33 posture?
```

---

## 23. How a Reviewer Should Use the Encyclopedia

A reviewer should audit:

```text
authority class
source evidence
role names
runtime posture
production claim boundaries
mutation boundaries
receipt availability
test coverage
release artifact integrity
```

Reviewer default stance:

```text
If authority is unclear, HOLD.
If source evidence is missing, NEEDS_SOURCE.
If contradiction exists, ESCALATE.
If production claim appears early, BLOCK.
```

---

## 24. Builder Failure Modes

Common builder failures:

```text
flattening ION into documentation
flattening ION into memory/RAG
flattening ION into a chatbot
flattening ION into a daemon
flattening ION into a release zip
promoting demo proof to production authority
using stale role names
rewriting source summaries directly
treating agent output as truth
skipping adversarial audit
```

The builder guide exists to prevent these.

## 25. Implementation Roadmap Table

| Phase | Build | Output | Production claim |
|---|---|---|---|
| V34 | A3 surface ratification | authority matrix | no |
| V35 | demo/primitive split | generic primitives | no |
| V36 | graph canon | graph authority | no/partial |
| V37 | summary rewrite proposal | proposal-only | no |
| V38 | summary commit/rollback | governed summary mutation | partial |
| V39 | agent activation protocol | activation requests/leases | no autonomous fan-out |
| V40 | subagent fan-out/fan-in | bounded distributed work | partial |
| V41 | daemon runtime | safe daemon candidate | no until audit |
| V42 | front-door product | product interface candidate | no until audit |
| V43 | adversarial audit | audit reports | maybe release-candidate-ready |
| V44 | production release candidate | production RC | candidate only |
| V45 | production verifier | verified production release | yes if passed |

## 26. Chapter Insert for Full Encyclopedia

## Chapter: The Encyclopedia Must Be Rebuildable

The production encyclopedia is not merely a book about ION. It is a recovery instrument.

ION’s history proves why this matters. When authority, templates, names, runtime surfaces, and release evidence drift apart, the system becomes difficult to trust. A future AI builder may read a smooth document and think it understands ION, while silently missing the difference between a demo proof and production authority, or between historical names and current truenames, or between bounded graph-state commit and canonical graph canon.

Therefore the encyclopedia must be rebuildable. It must give tracks, files, tests, commands, boundaries, and acceptance criteria. It must say not only what ION is, but how to reconstruct it from zero, how to continue from V33, how to verify the certified demo baseline, and how to know when production readiness has not yet been reached.

A builder should be able to enter at the conceptual layer, kernel layer, evented runtime layer, front-door layer, release-demo layer, or production layer and still find the same organism.

The correct standard is:

```text
A future AI builder can reconstruct ION’s doctrine, runtime spine, certified demo path, production-readiness gates, and remaining production sequence without hidden oral context.
```

If the encyclopedia can do that, it has become part of ION’s continuity engine.

---

```

```

## 19. Chapter Insert for Full Encyclopedia

## Chapter: Consistency Is a Production Surface

ION’s documentation cannot be treated as secondary. In ION, documentation is part of the operating substrate. A stale explanation can create stale context. A smooth overclaim can become a future agent’s false premise. A historical role name can reenter live authority if it is not marked. A demo proof can become production mythology if the encyclopedia does not preserve the boundary.

Therefore consistency is not cosmetic. It is operational.

The production encyclopedia must preserve exact posture: V10 is a runtime milestone, V32 is the certified demo baseline, V33 is the current production-readiness frame, and ION is not yet production-ready. It must preserve the role split of Persona Interface, Relay, and Steward. It must mark Codex historical-only. It must keep graph canon, source-summary rewrite, agent activation, daemon safety, and production release verification blocked until their gates pass.

A consistency audit is the mechanism that prevents a great document from becoming a dangerous one.

---

The next encyclopedia artifact should be:

ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_DRAFT_ASSEMBLY_PLAN.md

Purpose:

```text
define exact assembly strategy for the full v2.0 draft:
- volume/chapter ordering
- inclusion order for current draft parts
- old encyclopedia body mapping
- stale-language rewrite pass
- claim-tag insertion pass
- appendix structure
- final audit and release-candidate path
```


---

# Appendix — Draft Assembly Plan

## 1. Assembly Goal

The goal is to assemble the first full:

```text
ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_DRAFT.md
```

This draft should combine:

```text
1. the current v2.0 production encyclopedia parts
2. preserved and corrected material from the older evented living context graph encyclopedia
3. new production-readiness framing
4. runtime lineage V10–V33
5. ratification matrix
6. graph canon doctrine
7. source-summary rewrite doctrine
8. agent/subagent doctrine
9. daemon doctrine
10. front-door product doctrine
11. release engineering doctrine
12. builder implementation guide
```

The assembled draft is not a release candidate. It is a full working draft ready for post-assembly audit.

---

## 2. Non-Negotiable Assembly Posture

Every assembled draft must preserve:

```text
V10 = first bounded evented-template graph commit milestone
V32 = certified demo baseline
V33 = production-readiness frame
current verdict = NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
next production gate = V34_A3_SURFACE_RATIFICATION_PASS
```

Forbidden assembled-draft claims:

```text
ION is production-ready.
ION has ratified global graph canon.
ION can safely rewrite canonical source summaries.
ION can autonomously activate subagents.
ION has production daemon authority.
ION has a verified production release.
All A3 surfaces are ratified.
```

---

The assembly should draw from these current v2.0 artifacts:

If the old source is unavailable during assembly, the first v2.0 full draft should still proceed from the current v2.0 parts and mark old-body merge as pending.

---

## 4. Assembly Strategy

The assembly should not blindly concatenate the current parts.

The correct method is:

```text
front matter
→ claims ledger
→ source ledger
→ product definition
→ runtime lineage
→ production readiness
→ ratification matrix
→ technical architecture parts
→ product/release/builder parts
→ appendices
→ assembly receipt
```

Each imported part should be normalized:

```text
remove duplicate receipt blocks from body or move to appendix
normalize headings
preserve status lines
deduplicate repeated definitions
merge repeated boundary statements into one canonical boundary table
preserve all next-lawful-move references in appendix
```

---

---

## 6. Old Encyclopedia Merge Map

The old source encyclopedia should be merged cautiously.

## 6.1 Preserve with minimal rewrite

Preserve sections that define:

```text
living context graph
files as graph objects
templates as lawful forms
packets
receipts
registries
bounded context
front-door role split
historical correction that Codex is historical-only
```

Apply status tags and V33 posture.

## 6.2 Preserve but reframe

Reframe sections about:

```text
V10 current runtime
V11/V12 future path
evented graph implementation as current endpoint
candidate runtime surfaces that are now superseded by V17–V33
```

## 6.3 Move to historical appendix

Move old material about:

```text
donor-line names
Seedsonnet authority
Codex live orchestration
older branch conflicts
minified branch lineage
```

unless directly relevant to current authority correction.

## 6.4 Replace with new v2.0 parts

Replace old partial sections on:

```text
production readiness
ratification
release engineering
agent/subagent scaling
daemon runtime
graph canon
source-summary rewrite
builder guide
```

with the current v2.0 drafts.

## 6.5 Mark for contradiction review

Flag any old passage claiming or implying:

```text
production readiness
global graph canon
source rewrite authority
autonomous agent activation
current Codex authority
V10 as current endpoint
```

---

## 7. Stale-Language Rewrite Pass

The assembly must run a stale-language pass.

Search terms:

```text
Codex
Seedsonnet
V10 current
current V10
production-ready
global graph canon
source rewrite
summary rewrite
autonomous agents
agent swarm
daemon automation
release production
```

Rewrite rules:

```text
Codex -> historical-only unless historical context explicitly stated
Seedsonnet -> historical/donor label unless current semantic audit says otherwise
V10 current -> V10 runtime milestone
production-ready -> NOT_PRODUCTION_READY unless future/V44/V45 context
global graph canon -> blocked until V36
source rewrite -> blocked until V37–V38
autonomous agents/swarm -> blocked until V39–V40
daemon automation -> graph-aware daemon blocked until V41
production release -> blocked until V44/V45
```

---

## 8. Claims-Tag Insertion Pass

Every major claim must be tagged or placed under a tagged section.

Required tags:

```text
[A1-CROWN]
[A2-GOVERNANCE]
[A3-PROPOSAL]
[A4-DEMO]
[RUNTIME-PROVEN]
[DEMO-PROVEN]
[PRODUCTION-GATED]
[PROVISIONAL]
[HISTORICAL-ONLY]
[DEPRECATED]
[ASPIRATIONAL]
```

Examples:

```text
[PROVISIONAL] ION is a living context graph operated by lawful agents through templates.
[RUNTIME-PROVEN] V32 verifies existing demo release-candidate capsules.
[PRODUCTION-GATED] Source-summary rewrite authority remains blocked until V37–V38.
[HISTORICAL-ONLY] Codex is historical carrier/chassis lineage in the current authority frame.
```

---

## 9. Deduplication Rules

Because the v2.0 parts intentionally repeat boundaries, the final draft should deduplicate repeated text.

## 9.1 Keep one canonical boundary table near front

The front matter should include:

```text
not production-ready
V32 baseline
V33 frame
V34 next gate
blocked graph/source/agent/daemon/production release claims
```

## 9.2 Preserve local reminders

Each technical part may retain a short local reminder, but not full repeated posture blocks.

## 9.3 Move receipts to appendix

Draft receipts should not interrupt the main encyclopedia body. Move them to Appendix A.

## 9.4 Move next-lawful-move chain to appendix

Each part’s next artifact references should be consolidated in Appendix C.

---

## 10. Assembly Algorithm

The assembly agent should perform:

```text
1. create new file ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_DRAFT.md
2. write title/status/source block
3. import polished preface
4. import claims ledger
5. import source ledger
6. import volume/chapter table of contents
7. import each v2.0 part in volume order
8. normalize headings to chapter numbering
9. move receipts to appendix
10. deduplicate repeated status blocks
11. insert old encyclopedia preserved material under mapped volumes
12. apply stale-language rewrite pass
13. apply claims-tag pass
14. create appendix material
15. create draft assembly receipt
16. create manifest
17. run post-assembly consistency audit
```

---

## 11. Draft Assembly Receipt Schema

```yaml
draft_assembly_receipt:
  receipt_id:
  emitted_at:
  assembled_document:
  source_parts: []
  old_source_included:
    included: false
    source_path:
    merge_scope:
  production_claim: false
  production_verdict: NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
  certified_demo_baseline: V32
  production_readiness_frame: V33
  stale_language_scan:
    performed: true
    findings: []
  claims_tag_pass:
    performed: true
    major_claims_tagged: true
  post_assembly_audit_required: true
  next_lawful_move: ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_POST_ASSEMBLY_CONSISTENCY_AUDIT.md
```

---

## 12. Post-Assembly Audit Requirements

After `ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_DRAFT.md` is created, run:

```text
ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_POST_ASSEMBLY_CONSISTENCY_AUDIT.md
```

Audit checks:

```text
V10 posture
V32 posture
V33 posture
NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
Codex historical-only
Persona/Relay/Steward split
graph canon blocked until V36
source-summary rewrite blocked until V37–V38
agent activation blocked until V39–V40
daemon blocked until V41
front-door productization blocked until V42
production release blocked until V44/V45
claims tags present
old-body contradictions resolved or marked
receipts in appendix
manifest complete
```

---

## 13. Draft Assembly Acceptance Criteria

The draft assembly is acceptable when:

```text
1. all v2.0 draft parts are represented
2. volume order follows this plan
3. production verdict remains NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
4. V10/V32/V33 posture is preserved
5. old body is not merged unfiltered
6. stale language is rewritten or flagged
7. claims tags are applied
8. receipts are moved to appendix
9. all major gates are represented
10. next artifact is post-assembly consistency audit
```

---

## 14. Release Candidate Path After Draft Assembly

After full draft assembly:

```text
ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_DRAFT.md
→ ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_POST_ASSEMBLY_CONSISTENCY_AUDIT.md
→ ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_REVIEW_PATCHSET.md
→ ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_RELEASE_CANDIDATE.md
→ ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_RELEASE_CANDIDATE_VERIFIER.md
```

The encyclopedia release candidate is a documentation release candidate, not an ION production release.

---

## 15. What the Full Draft Should Not Do

The full draft should not:

```text
claim ION production readiness
pretend V34–V45 have been completed
erase historical contradictions
hide old donor names without mapping
inflate release-demo proof
merge all receipts into prose
omit claim tags
omit production gaps
skip post-assembly audit
```

---

## 16. Chapter Insert for Full Encyclopedia

## Chapter: Assembly Is a Governed Operation

The production encyclopedia is now large enough that assembling it is itself a governed operation. A final draft cannot be produced by simply concatenating previous documents. Each part contains boundary statements, receipts, next-lawful moves, repeated status notes, and technical doctrine. The assembler must preserve the meaning while reducing duplication and preventing old-language relapse.

The assembly plan therefore defines volume order, source order, old-body merge rules, stale-language rewrite rules, claims-tag requirements, appendix structure, and post-assembly audit requirements.

This is not bureaucracy. It is continuity protection. If the encyclopedia is assembled incorrectly, future agents may inherit a smooth but false picture of ION. If it is assembled lawfully, the encyclopedia becomes a recovery surface: a document that can teach, rebuild, audit, and continue ION without hidden oral context.

The correct next action is not a release candidate. It is a full draft followed by post-assembly consistency audit.

---

## 17. Next Artifact

The next encyclopedia artifact should be:

```text
ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_DRAFT.md
```

Then immediately:

```text
ION_Production_Encyclopedia_v2_0_POST_ASSEMBLY_CONSISTENCY_AUDIT.md
```

# V42 Seed — Conversational Receipts and Live Repair

## Purpose

This v2.2 encyclopedia continuation records the next lawful branch declared by the V41 project evidence:

```text
V42_CONVERSATIONAL_RECEIPTS_AND_LIVE_REPAIR
```

V42 is not asserted as implemented in the inspected live project packet. It is the successor target named by the V41 handoff and policy. Its function is to carry V41's claim-class receipt machinery into the actual tempo of live conversation, especially voice/video Persona workflows where the user-facing surface must respond quickly while Relay, Steward/VZ, graph lookup, visual inspection, or specialist agents may still be resolving evidence.

V41 made the front-stage claim receipt executable. V42 should make conversational repair executable.

The distinction is critical:

```text
V41 asks: may this user-facing claim be emitted as phrased?
V42 asks: what happens when a fast conversational utterance must later be corrected, narrowed, repaired, or upgraded?
```

ION's live Persona must be able to speak without becoming theatrical. It must also be able to repair itself without pretending the repair never happened. V42 is the branch that should turn that behavior into a receipt surface.

---

## V42 Receipt

```yaml
receipt_id: ion-production-encyclopedia-v2-2-v42-conversational-receipts-seed-20260426
receipt_class: encyclopedia_successor_branch_seed
authority_posture: A3_DESIGN_SEED_FROM_LIVE_V41_HANDOFF
production_claim: false
runtime_implementation_claim: false
live_project_claim: false
source_evidence:
  - ION/05_context/handoff/V41_FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_SUCCESSOR_HANDOFF.md
  - ION/03_registry/front_stage_council_runtime_policy.yaml
  - ION/02_architecture/LIVE_PERSONA_LATENCY_AND_PROVISIONAL_UTTERANCE_PROTOCOL.md
  - ION/02_architecture/FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_RUNTIME_RECEIPT_PROTOCOL.md
  - ION/04_packages/kernel/front_stage_council_receipt.py
successor_target: V42_CONVERSATIONAL_RECEIPTS_AND_LIVE_REPAIR
claim_boundary:
  - V42 is declared as next lawful move by V41 evidence
  - this encyclopedia section designs the target
  - this section does not implement V42 in the ION project tree
  - this section does not grant production authority
```

---

## Why V42 Is Necessary

V41 solves a core representational problem: the Persona cannot simply emit claims because they sound fluent. Claims must be classified, grounded, authorized, scoped, blocked, or repaired. But V41 is still oriented around a claim object. Live conversation is more fluid than a single claim object.

A live Persona may produce:

```text
backchannels
partial acknowledgements
fast summaries
interruption handling
low-confidence first reads
mid-answer updates
self-corrections
late-arriving Relay evidence
late-arriving Steward/VZ restrictions
visual observations arriving after a preliminary answer
file/test evidence arriving after an initial synthesis
user corrections that change the target
```

Without V42, these events may remain conversationally visible but structurally lost. The Persona might correct itself, but the correction would not necessarily become durable state. Future agents might inherit the repaired statement but not the fact that a repair occurred, why it occurred, what evidence triggered it, or what claim was invalidated.

V42 should make the repair path explicit.

The governing principle:

```text
A correction is not merely an apology. A correction is a continuity event.
```

If ION is to maintain work honestly, it must preserve not only final answers but also the repair mechanics that protected the work from drift.

---

## Relationship to V41

V42 should not replace the V41 Front-Stage Council Receipt. It should wrap conversational sequences around V41 receipts.

The recommended relationship is:

```text
utterance event
→ provisional lane classification
→ optional or required V41 claim receipt
→ delayed evidence update if needed
→ repair/retraction/narrowing/upgrade event
→ final repaired claim receipt
→ continuation obligation
```

V41 receipt fields remain fundamental:

```text
claim_class
persona_state
relay_state
steward_verdict
risk_level
emission_permission
visibility_level
repair_required
repair_obligations
production_authority=false
```

V42 should add conversational lifecycle fields:

```text
conversation_turn_id
utterance_id
latency_lane
provisional_status
superseded_by
repair_type
repair_trigger
repair_visibility
continuation_effect
```

V41 classifies claim authority. V42 records how claim authority changes across time.

---

## Conversational Lifecycle States

V42 should define a lifecycle for user-facing speech.

Candidate states:

```yaml
DRAFTING:
  meaning: Persona is composing internally; no user-facing utterance has been emitted.

PROVISIONAL_EMITTED:
  meaning: Persona emitted a low-risk or bounded utterance before full ratification.

CHECK_PENDING:
  meaning: Relay, Steward/VZ, graph, test, visual, or specialist evidence is still pending.

CHECKED_STABLE:
  meaning: The utterance is supported by sufficient evidence for its claim class.

NARROWED:
  meaning: A prior utterance was too broad and has been narrowed without fully reversing it.

CORRECTED:
  meaning: A prior utterance contained an error and has been corrected.

RETRACTED:
  meaning: A prior utterance should not be used as a basis for continuation.

UPGRADED:
  meaning: A provisional or proposed statement became better supported after evidence arrived.

BLOCKED:
  meaning: The utterance cannot be emitted or preserved as phrased.

SETTLED:
  meaning: The conversational sequence has a final claim boundary and continuation state.
```

These states allow ION to distinguish several cases that normal chat collapses:

```text
“I was right but too broad.”
“I was wrong and corrected it.”
“I was speculative and later verified it.”
“I was speculative and later blocked it.”
“I was conversationally supportive but made no durable claim.”
“I started to answer, then stopped because the evidence contradicted the phrasing.”
```

For ION, these are not stylistic variations. They are different continuity events.

---

## Repair Types

V42 should classify repairs by type.

Candidate repair taxonomy:

```yaml
SCOPE_NARROWING:
  definition: The original statement was directionally valid but too broad.
  example: “I should narrow that: the focused tests passed, not the full suite.”

FACT_CORRECTION:
  definition: The original statement was false or unsupported.
  example: “Correction: that file is not present in the live root.”

AUTHORITY_DOWNGRADE:
  definition: A claim was phrased as settled but must be represented as proposal, speculation, or unverified relay content.
  example: “That should be framed as a design seed, not a landed protocol.”

AUTHORITY_UPGRADE:
  definition: New evidence supports stronger representation than was initially allowed.
  example: “Now verified: the V41 receipt module exists and focused tests pass.”

EVIDENCE_REFRESH:
  definition: Older evidence became stale and was replaced by a newer inspection.
  example: “The earlier V33 framing is superseded by the V41 packet.”

VISUAL_RECHECK:
  definition: Rendered or visual evidence changed the state of a claim.
  example: “The source patch existed, but the rendered UI still failed the expected behavior.”

USER_CORRECTION_ACCEPTED:
  definition: The user supplied a correction that changes the live target or authority surface.
  example: “The live root is the encyclopedia packet, not the canvas.”

FORBIDDEN_REPRESENTATION_REPAIR:
  definition: A phrasing implied forbidden identity, authority, production readiness, hidden memory, or unrestricted control.
  example: “I should not represent the Persona as the totality of ION.”

PRODUCTION_CLAIM_REPAIR:
  definition: A statement implied production readiness or verification beyond evidence.
  example: “The artifact is updated, but production authority remains false.”
```

This taxonomy should be tested directly against ION's own recent workflow because the current interaction exposed exactly the class of error V42 exists to handle: the assistant created and emphasized a canvas when the authoritative target was the Markdown artifact. In V42 terms, that was a `USER_CORRECTION_ACCEPTED` event followed by `AUTHORITY_DOWNGRADE` of the canvas and `EVIDENCE_REFRESH` against the encyclopedia packet.

---

## V42 Conversational Receipt Object

The recommended core object is `ConversationalRepairReceipt`.

Candidate schema:

```yaml
schema_id: ion.conversational_repair_receipt.v1
version: V42_CONVERSATIONAL_RECEIPTS_AND_LIVE_REPAIR
receipt_id: string
conversation_id: string | null
turn_id: string | null
utterance_id: string
created_at: timestamp
source_utterance: string
source_claim_class: C0 | C1 | C2 | C3 | C4 | C5 | NONE
source_latency_lane: L0 | L1 | L2 | L3 | L4
source_emission_permission: string | null
repair_required: boolean
repair_type: enum
repair_trigger: enum
repair_visibility: QUIET | EXPANDABLE | MANDATORY | BLOCKING
repair_text: string
repaired_claim_text: string | null
repaired_claim_class: C0 | C1 | C2 | C3 | C4 | C5 | NONE
linked_v41_receipt_before: string | null
linked_v41_receipt_after: string | null
evidence_delta:
  added: list
  contradicted: list
  stale: list
  missing: list
continuation_effect:
  invalidates_prior_claim: boolean
  updates_next_action: boolean
  requires_artifact_patch: boolean
  requires_user_visibility: boolean
production_authority: false
```

The `production_authority` field must remain `false` by constant. V42 is a repair and continuity surface, not production authorization.

---

## V42 and Latency Lanes

The live Persona latency protocol already defines lanes:

```text
L0 — backchannel
L1 — conversational provisional
L2 — checked response
L3 — ratified answer
L4 — formal artifact
```

V42 should enforce a lane-to-receipt policy:

```yaml
L0_BACKCHANNEL:
  receipt_required_by_default: false
  receipt_required_when:
    - backchannel accidentally includes substantive claim
    - user correction targets the utterance

L1_CONVERSATIONAL_PROVISIONAL:
  receipt_required_by_default: optional
  receipt_required_when:
    - utterance affects durable work state
    - later evidence changes it
    - user-facing correction is needed

L2_CHECKED_RESPONSE:
  receipt_required_by_default: true_for_substantive_claims
  linked_v41_receipt: recommended

L3_RATIFIED_ANSWER:
  receipt_required_by_default: true
  linked_v41_receipt: required

L4_FORMAL_ARTIFACT:
  receipt_required_by_default: true
  linked_v41_receipt: required
  artifact_patch_receipt: required_if_changed
```

This resolves the tension between conversational speed and auditability. Low-risk speech remains fast. Durable work state remains receipted.

---

## V42 and Markdown/Artifact Work

Because the live root for the encyclopedia is a Markdown packet, V42 must explicitly govern artifact-facing repairs.

Artifact repair should be more stringent than ordinary chat correction. If a conversational correction changes a Markdown artifact, V42 should require:

```text
1. identify the mistaken or stale artifact claim;
2. classify the repair type;
3. patch the Markdown file;
4. create a receipt for the patch;
5. update manifest/checksum surfaces;
6. preserve production_claim=false unless separately ratified;
7. return the artifact link to the user.
```

The recent correction “stop making a canvas; update the Markdown file” should therefore become a canonical V42 example:

```yaml
example_id: v42_artifact_surface_correction_canvas_to_md
source_error: assistant treated side canvas as working artifact
user_correction: live root is the ION Production Encyclopedia Markdown packet
repair_type:
  - USER_CORRECTION_ACCEPTED
  - AUTHORITY_DOWNGRADE
  - ARTIFACT_TARGET_REALIGNMENT
required_action:
  - stop using canvas as authority
  - update encyclopedia Markdown packet
  - preserve receipt of correction
  - return updated zip and direct MD
```

This example is valuable because it demonstrates ION's principle in practice: the system must not defend the wrong substrate. It must re-anchor to the authoritative artifact.

---

## V42 and Visual Perception

V42 must also integrate with the Visual Perception and Interaction Agent.

Visual evidence often arrives after an initial utterance. For example:

```text
Persona: “The UI likely renders correctly based on the component code.”
Visual Agent: screenshot shows overflow and broken alignment.
V42 repair: authority downgrade and visual recheck correction.
```

The repair receipt should preserve:

```yaml
repair_trigger: VISUAL_EVIDENCE_CONTRADICTION
source_claim: source_code_implies_correct_render
new_evidence: screenshot_or_dom_read_inspection
repair_type:
  - VISUAL_RECHECK
  - FACT_CORRECTION
  - AUTHORITY_DOWNGRADE
repaired_claim: source code exists, but rendered behavior does not yet pass visual verification
continuation_effect:
  requires_patch_request: true
  requires_post_patch_verify: true
```

This makes the live product rule operational:

```text
Rendered behavior is part of truth. Source-code correctness is not product correctness.
```

V42 is the mechanism that allows a fast code-based inference to be corrected by later visual evidence without losing continuity.

---

## V42 and Claim-Class Conversion

V42 should record claim-class conversions explicitly.

Examples:

```yaml
C0_to_C2:
  meaning: A statement represented as direct verified state was downgraded to proposal.
  visibility: MANDATORY if user-facing work depended on it.

C1_to_C0:
  meaning: A strong derived interpretation was later verified directly.
  visibility: EXPANDABLE unless high-impact.

C2_to_C0:
  meaning: A design candidate was implemented and verified.
  visibility: MANDATORY for release or artifact claims.

C3_to_C2:
  meaning: Speculation became a design proposal.
  visibility: EXPANDABLE.

C4_to_BLOCKED:
  meaning: Unverified relay content cannot be emitted as known.
  visibility: BLOCKING if response depends on it.

C5_to_REPAIRED:
  meaning: Forbidden representation was replaced with allowed language.
  visibility: MANDATORY or BLOCKING depending on severity.
```

This conversion ledger prevents future agents from inheriting only the final wording. They inherit the epistemic movement.

---

## V42 Minimum File Set

If implemented in the ION project tree, V42 should add at least:

```text
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V42_CONVERSATIONAL_RECEIPTS_AND_LIVE_REPAIR_LOCK.md
ION/02_architecture/CONVERSATIONAL_RECEIPTS_AND_LIVE_REPAIR_PROTOCOL.md
ION/03_registry/conversational_repair_receipt.schema.json
ION/03_registry/conversational_repair_policy.yaml
ION/04_packages/kernel/conversational_repair_receipt.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_conversational_repair_receipt.py
ION/05_context/handoff/V42_CONVERSATIONAL_REPAIR_SUCCESSOR_HANDOFF.md
```

Optional but recommended:

```text
ION/07_templates/conversation/CONVERSATIONAL_REPAIR_RECEIPT.md
ION/07_templates/conversation/PROVISIONAL_UTTERANCE_LOG.md
ION/07_templates/conversation/USER_CORRECTION_ACCEPTANCE_RECEIPT.md
ION/07_templates/conversation/ARTIFACT_TARGET_REALIGNMENT_RECEIPT.md
ION/07_templates/visual/VISUAL_RECHECK_REPAIR_RECEIPT.md
```

These should remain A3/runtime-inspection until ratified.

---

## Candidate Kernel Decision Logic

The V42 kernel should not need to be large. It can begin as a deterministic classifier that receives:

```text
source utterance
source claim class
latency lane
new evidence status
user correction status
artifact impact
risk level
linked V41 receipt
```

and returns:

```text
repair_required
repair_type
repair_visibility
repair_text requirement
continuation obligations
```

Pseudo-logic:

```text
if source claim is C5:
    block, require forbidden-representation repair
elif user correction changes artifact target:
    require artifact-target realignment receipt
elif new evidence contradicts emitted claim:
    require fact correction or scope narrowing
elif evidence upgrades proposal/speculation to verified state:
    allow authority upgrade with receipt
elif utterance was low-risk backchannel with no durable claim:
    no repair required
else:
    preserve current V41 emission permission
```

The goal is not to mechanize all language judgment. The goal is to ensure that once a repair condition is recognized, it has an explicit path.

---

## V42 Test Plan

The first V42 test suite should include at least these cases:

```text
1. L0 backchannel without substantive claim does not require receipt.
2. L1 provisional utterance later contradicted by Relay requires correction receipt.
3. C0 claim without grounding downgraded to C2 or blocked.
4. User correction that changes artifact target requires artifact-target realignment receipt.
5. Visual evidence contradiction requires visual recheck repair.
6. C5 forbidden representation blocks and requires repair.
7. Authority upgrade from C2 to C0 requires linked after-receipt.
8. Artifact-facing repair requires manifest/checksum update obligation.
9. Production authority remains false in all V42 receipts.
10. V42 receipt cannot override a V41 blocked-forbidden-representation verdict.
```

These tests should be narrow, deterministic, and focused on receipts rather than broad agent behavior.

---

## V42 Encyclopedia Canon Rules

This pass adds the following V42 seed rules to the encyclopedia:

```text
1. A correction is a continuity event.

2. Fast speech is allowed only when its claim boundary is repairable.

3. V41 classifies claim emission; V42 records claim repair across conversational time.

4. A user correction that changes the authoritative work surface must be receipted as artifact-target realignment.

5. Visual evidence can trigger conversational repair when rendered behavior contradicts source-based inference.

6. Claim-class movement must be recorded, not hidden inside the final answer.

7. Retraction is not failure when it is timely, scoped, and receipted.

8. Artifact-facing repairs require artifact patches, receipts, manifests, and checksums.

9. V42 does not grant production authority.

10. The next agent must inherit both the repaired claim and the reason repair occurred.
```

---

## Settlement

This v2.2 continuation settles V42 as the correct next encyclopedia design target because it is declared by live V41 evidence. It does not claim V42 has landed in the live project root.

```yaml
settled:
  - V42_CONVERSATIONAL_RECEIPTS_AND_LIVE_REPAIR is the next live successor target declared by V41 evidence
  - V42 should extend V41 from claim-emission receipts into conversational repair receipts
  - V42 should explicitly support user corrections, mid-answer repairs, retractions, scope narrowing, authority downgrade/upgrade, visual recheck, and artifact-target realignment
  - this encyclopedia packet should preserve the canvas-to-Markdown correction as a canonical V42 example

not_settled:
  - actual V42 project implementation
  - exact schema finalization
  - kernel module code
  - test suite landing in project root
  - production authority
  - release readiness
```

The next lawful encyclopedia step after this seed is to produce a dedicated section:

```text
CONVERSATIONAL_RECEIPTS_AND_LIVE_REPAIR_PROTOCOL_DRAFT
```

and then, if project mutation is requested, to land the V42 file set into the ION project tree with focused tests and non-production receipts.
